id="endocrinology">ENDOCRINOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endocrinology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 <p>H. Kibicho</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By the end of the unit the students should be able to describe:</p>
<p>a. Anatomy and physiology of endocrine system
b. Assessment of the endocrine system
c. Describe various endocrine disorders under the headings:</p>
<p>Definition, clinical features, medical, nursing and surgical interventions</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-endocrine-system">THE ENDOCRINE SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>“endo” means within.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endocrine system is a system of ductless glands that secrete hormones. The glands are widely separated with no anatomical links.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is a chemical control system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It functions in conjunction with the nervous system to control the internal environment (homeostasis).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These glands consist of secretory cells which secrete hormones and dense network of capillaries which carries hormones in blood</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Glands: specialized tissues that produce a hormone or product.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hormones: chemical messengers produced by ductless/endocrine glands which flow directly into the blood where they are carried to another organ to influence activity, growth and nutrition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hormones together with the ANS regulate the internal environment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rapid action by the nervous system is balanced by slower hormonal action...permitting precise control of organ functions in response to varied changes within and outside the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endocrine glands</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are composed of secretory cells arranged in minute clusters known as acini.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are ductless</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Have a rich blood supply so that the hormones they produce enter the bloodstream rapidly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Secrete chemicals known as hormones</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endocrine glands produce a variety of hormones which drive very different processes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Many glands are controlled by the Hypothalamus and Pituitary glands.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endocrine glands are</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 pituitary gland</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 thyroid gland</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>4 parathyroid glands</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2 adrenal/suprarenal glands</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The pancreatic islets (islets of langerhans)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 pineal gland or body</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 thymus gland</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2 ovaries in the female</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2 testes in the male</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Copyright © The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. Permission required for reproduction or display.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-endocrine-system">The Endocrine System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-26a7e106.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Define the following terms and give examples of each
a) Endocrine glands
b) Exocrine glands
c) Autocrine glands
d) Paracrine glands
e) Juxtacrine glands</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Define the following terms
a) Hormones
b) Neurohormones
c) Pherohormones
d) Interleukins
e) Interferons</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>The glands are called <strong>ductless</strong> (do not have ducts to carry secretions) because hormones diffuse directly into the blood stream</li>
<li>This differentiate them from exocrine glands eg sweat gland</li>
<li>The major glands are: Pituitary gland, Thyroid gland, Parathyroid gland, Thymus gland, Adrenal gland, Testes and Ovaries</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5fea70e6.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principle-functions-of-endocrine-system">PRINCIPLE FUNCTIONS OF ENDOCRINE SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle-functions-of-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Growth, metabolism, &amp; tissue maturation by growth hormone</li>
<li>Ion regulation by parathyroid hormone</li>
<li>Heart rate &amp; blood pressure regulation</li>
<li>Blood glucose control by glucagon and insulin</li>
<li>Immune system regulation by thyroid hormone</li>
<li>Reproductive functions control by FSH and testosterone</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormones">HORMONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They are chemical released from living cells that travels some distance to target tissues to have a biological effect</li>
<li>They are chemical messengers</li>
<li>They are secreted in very small amounts and usually transported in the blood</li>
<li>They act on distant target cells</li>
<li>Target cells have specific receptors</li>
<li>The effects are dependent on the programmed response of the target cells</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>When hormones arrive at its target cell, it binds to a specific site, the receptor, where it acts to influence a chemical or metabolic reactions made inside the cell</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanisms-of-hormone-release">MECHANISMS OF HORMONE RELEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-hormone-release" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(a) Humoral: in response to changing levels of ions or nutrients in the blood
(b) Neural: stimulation by nerves
(c) Hormonal: stimulation received from other hormones</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormonal-mode-of-action">HORMONAL MODE OF ACTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-mode-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Hormones can act in two ways:</p>
<ol>
<li>Reversing the action of stimulus: negative feedback mechanism</li>
<li>Amplifying the stimulus; positive feedback mechanism</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-negative-feedback-mechanism">1. NEGATIVE FEEDBACK MECHANISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-negative-feedback-mechanism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs when the action of hormone stops its further release.</li>
<li>The stimulus causes a release of hormone which acts on a target organ or tissue and the resulting action of hormone tend to suppress its further release</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Example of negative feedback mechanism</li>
<li>Rising blood sugar stimulates pancreatic cells to release insulin.</li>
<li>insulin increases uptake of glucose hence lowering blood sugar.</li>
<li>When blood sugar is lowered, the production of insulin stops this leads rising blood sugar (humoral hormonal release)</li>
<li>Hormone released; insulin</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Resulting action of hormone : increase uptake of glucose</li>
<li>As a result of glucose uptake ; insulin release stops.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="positive-feedback-mechanism">POSITIVE FEEDBACK MECHANISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positive-feedback-mechanism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs when the action of hormone causes additional secretion of the same hormone.</li>
<li>Example: rising levels of Oxytocin stimulates contractions in the uterus.</li>
<li>Contractions in the uterus stimulate receptors in the pelvis which triggers the release of more Oxytocin for more contractions until child birth</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classes-of-hormones">CLASSES OF HORMONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classes-of-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Proteins and polypeptides e.g. hormone secreted by anterior and posterior pituitary gland, parathyroid hormone, insulin and glucagon</li>
<li>Steroids: hormones secreted by adrenal cortex e.g. cortisol, aldosterone, hormones secreted by ovaries e.g. estrogen and progesterone, hormone secreted by testes e.g. testosterone</li>
<li>Amines or amino acids: thyroid hormone, epinephrine and norepinephrine</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="endocrine-glands">ENDOCRINE GLANDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endocrine-glands" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Hypothalamus
(brain region controlling the pituitary gland)</p>
<p>Thyroid gland
(affects metabolism, among other things)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1ce5703a.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Pituitary gland
(secretes many different hormones, some of which affect other glands)</p>
<p>Parathyroids
(help regulate the level of calcium in the blood)</p>
<p>Adrenal glands
(inner part, called the medulla, helps trigger the "fight or flight" response)</p>
<p>Pancreas
(regulates the level of sugar in the blood)</p>
<p>Ovary
(secretes female sex hormones)</p>
<p>Testis
(secretes male sex hormones)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glands-of-endocrine-system">Glands of endocrine system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glands-of-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>1 Pituitary gland</li>
<li>1 Thyroid gland</li>
<li>4 Parathyroid glands</li>
<li>2 Adrenal (suprarenal) glands</li>
<li>The pancreatic islets (islets of langerhans)</li>
<li>1 Pineal gland or body</li>
<li>1 Thymus gland</li>
<li>2 Ovaries in the female</li>
<li>2 Testes in the male</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-pituitary-gland-and-hypothalamus">1. Pituitary gland and hypothalamus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-pituitary-gland-and-hypothalamus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-30f76087.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pituitary-gland-and-hypothalamus">Pituitary gland and hypothalamus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pituitary-gland-and-hypothalamus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Location: in Sella Turcica of sphenoid bone Attached to Hypothalamus by a stalk called Infundibulum</li>
<li>The pituitary gland and the hypothalamus act as a unit.</li>
<li>The hypothalamus has a direct controlling effect on the pituitary gland and an indirect effect on many others.</li>
<li>A sort of master gland. The real boss is the hypothalamus. It is divided into two;</li>
<li>Anterior lobe – [glandular part] Adenohypophysis</li>
<li>Posterior lobe – [neural part] – Neurohypophysis</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-anterior-pituitary-gland-adenohypophysis">1. Anterior pituitary gland (Adenohypophysis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-anterior-pituitary-gland-adenohypophysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It produces six (6) hormones. The hormones are;</p>
<p>I. Growth hormone(GH)</p>
<p>II. Thyroid stimulating hormone(TSH)</p>
<p>III. Adrenocorticotropic hormone-- (ACTH)</p>
<p>iv. Prolactin</p>
<p>v. Follicle Stimulating Hormone (FSH)</p>
<p>vi. Luteinizing Hormone.(LH)</p>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-posterior-pituitary-gland-neurohypophysis">2. Posterior pituitary gland (Neurohypophysis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-posterior-pituitary-gland-neurohypophysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Produces two (2) hormones.</p>
<p>i. Antidiuretic Hormone (ADH) (Vasopressin)</p>
<p>ii. Oxytocin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypothalamic-control-of-pituitary-gland-secretions">Hypothalamic control of pituitary gland secretions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothalamic-control-of-pituitary-gland-secretions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The anterior gland is controlled by hormones released by hypothalamus</li>
<li>These hormones are called hypothalamic releasing and inhibiting hormones</li>
<li>These hormones are released from hypothalamus and conducted to anterior pituitary gland through minute blood vessels called pituitary portal system</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Posterior pituitary gland is controlled by nerve signals that originate from hypothalamus and terminate in posterior pituitary</li>
<li>The release of hormones is triggered by excitation of the gland by nerve impulses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anterior-pituitary-gland">Anterior pituitary gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anterior-pituitary-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are six hormones secreted by anterior pituitary gland</li>
<li>These hormones play role in control of metabolic functions in the body</li>
<li>The release of anterior pituitary hormone follows stimulation of gland by specific releasing hormone produced by hypothalamus</li>
<li>The whole system is control by feedback mechanism</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>The six important hormones are</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Growth hormone</li>
<li>Thyroid stimulating hormone</li>
<li>Adrenocorticotropic hormone (ACTH)</li>
<li>Prolactin</li>
<li>Follicle stimulating hormone (FSH)</li>
<li>Luteinizing Hormone (LH)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-growth-hormone">1. GROWTH HORMONE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-growth-hormone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is also called somatotropic hormone</li>
<li>It's release stimulated by growth releasing hormone and suppressed by growth hormone releasing inhibiting hormone</li>
<li>It is stimulated by hypoglycemia, deep sleep, fasting, exercise, and anxiety.</li>
<li>Peak release is reached in adolescence</li>
<li>It is inhibited by hyperglycemia, glucocorticoids, dihydrotestosterone,</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Inhibition is by negative feedback mechanism</li>
<li>Major target of the hormone are body cells, bones and skeletal muscle tissues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-growth-hormone">Functions of growth hormone<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-growth-hormone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Regulates metabolism-by protein synthesis, use of fats for fuel and conservation of glucose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>promote growth of bones and muscles</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thyroid stimulating Hormone</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Is also called thyrotropin</li>
<li>Its release is stimulated by thyroid releasing hormone from hypothalamus.</li>
<li>Its target is thyroid gland</li>
<li>Function: it stimulate thyroid gland to release thyroxine (T4) and Tri-iodothyronine (T3)</li>
<li>Secretion is regulated by negative feedback mechanism</li>
<li>When blood levels of thyroid hormones is high, secretion of TSH is reduced</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>ADRENOCORTICOTROPIC HORMONE (ACTH)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Its release is triggered by corticotrophin releasing hormone from the hypothalamus</li>
<li>Function: ACTH stimulates adrenal cortex to secrete glucocorticoid hormones especially cortisol</li>
<li>Secretion is regulated by negative feedback mechanism</li>
<li>Other factors that stimulate secretion include hypoglycemia, exercise and stress</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Prolactin</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Stimulate lactation (milk production) immediately after birth.</li>
<li>Its release is stimulated by Prolactin releasing hormone from hypothalamus and it is lowered by Prolactin inhibiting hormone</li>
<li>After birth, suckling stimulates Prolactin secretion and lactation</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>FOLLICLE STIMULATING HORMONE</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Stimulate maturation of ovarian follicles.</li>
<li>Stimulates secretion of estrogen by ovaries</li>
<li>Stimulates production of sperm in testes.</li>
<li>Secreted in puberty</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>LUTEINISING HORMONE (LH)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Necessary for final follicular growth and ovulation</li>
<li>Stimulates secretion of progesterone by corpus luteum and secretion of testosterone in males testis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="posterior-pituitary-gland">POSTERIOR PITUITARY GLAND<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#posterior-pituitary-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Produces two hormones</p>
<ul>
<li>Oxytocin</li>
<li>Antidiuretic Hormone (ADH)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-oxytocin">1. Oxytocin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-oxytocin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Main targets are breast and uterus.</li>
<li>Are released during childbirth into the uterus to stimulate uterine contractions and stretching of uterine cervix as the baby is expelled.</li>
<li>Its controlled by positive feedback mechanism.</li>
<li>Stimulate glandular cells and ducts of lactating breast to eject milk.</li>
<li>The process of milk ejection also involves positive feedback mechanism.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Anti-Diuretic Hormone (ADH)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Also called vasopressin</li>
<li>It stimulates the distal convoluted tubules of the KIDNEYS nephrone to reabsorb more water hence leading to decrease urine output</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d52c03ca.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Blood levels exert regulatory influences upon the anterior pituitary gland and the hypothalamus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thyroid-gland">Thyroid gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroid-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Highly vascularised gland located in front of larynx at 5th, 6th, 7th cervical and 1st thoracic vertebrae (C5, C6, C7 and T1 vertebrae)</li>
<li>It's made up of two lobes</li>
<li>Blood is supplied through inferior and superior thyroid arteries.</li>
<li>Venous return is by thyroid veins</li>
<li>There are two parathyroid glands laying at posterior surface of each lobe</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b5a32348.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>It is innervated by recurrent laryngeal nerve</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thyroid-hormones">THYROID HORMONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroid-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There three major thyroid hormones- thyroxine (T4) Tri-iodothyronine (T3) and calcitonin</li>
<li>T4 and T3 are together called thyroid hormone</li>
<li>Both hormones profoundly increases the rate of metabolism in the body.</li>
<li>Their release into the blood is stimulated by TSH from anterior pituitary gland</li>
<li>They are synthesized as large precursor molecules called thyroglobulin</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Stress, Malnutrition, Low plasma glucose and Exercises stimulate hypothalamus to release thyroid releasing Hormone (TRH)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once released, the TRH is sent to anterior pituitary gland which stimulate thyroid stimulating hormone (TSH)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TSH is sent to Thyroid gland to stimulate production of T3 and T4.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iodine react with tyrosine to form thyroid hormone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When supply of iodine is deficient, Excess TSH is secreted and there is proliferation of thyroid gland cells and enlargement of gland (goitre).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thyroxine (T4) is produced in large amounts as compared to T3, i.e. 93% of thyroid hormone is thyroxine and only 7% is T3.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>T3 is more potent than T4.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>25% of T4 is converted to T3 by de-iodination of T4 to T3.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hence the hormone delivered to tissues is mainly T3.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-thyroid-hormone">Functions of Thyroid hormone<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-thyroid-hormone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They are essential for normal growth and development</li>
<li>They regulate metabolism of carbohydrates, fats and proteins</li>
<li>Increases basal metabolic rate and heat production</li>
<li>Regulate expression of genes in the nucleus by increasing or decreasing synthesis of proteins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="calcitonin">CALCITONIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calcitonin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is secreted by <strong>parafollicular or C-cells</strong> of the thyroid gland when there is increased levels of calcium in the blood</li>
<li>It <strong>reduces calcium</strong> level in the plasma
a) stimulating calcium uptake in the bone matrix (deposition in the bones)
b) inhibit reabsorption of calcium in the kidney tubules</li>
<li>The hormone is important during childhood when bones undergo changes in size</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parathyroid-gland">Parathyroid gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parathyroid-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are four parathyroid glands, two in each lobe at posterior surface of the thyroid gland</li>
<li>They contain chief cells or principal cells which secrete parathyroid hormone.</li>
<li>Parathyroid hormone or parathormone is secreted when the blood calcium levels is low</li>
<li>Its main function is to increase ionic calcium in the blood plasma by:</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ol>
<li>Stimulating <strong>osteoclast</strong> in the bone to digest some of the bone matrix to release ionic calcium in the blood</li>
<li>Enhance reabsorption of calcium and excretion of phosphates by kidneys</li>
<li>Increases absorption of calcium by intestinal mucosa</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Vit D is required for absorption of ca+ in the intestine.</li>
<li>For vitamin D to facilitate absorption of Ca2+, it must be converted into Vit D3 form called calcitriol and this conversion is stimulated by PTH</li>
<li>Parathormone and Calcitonin act in opposite manner to regulate normal calcium levels required for muscle contraction, blood clotting and nerve impulse transmission.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrenal-glands">ADRENAL GLANDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrenal-glands" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Are located at the top of the kidneys.</li>
<li>Consists of two endocrine glands:</li>
<li>outer adrenal cortex</li>
<li>inner adrenal medulla.</li>
<li>The outer adrenal cortex act more of a gland while the inner medulla act as part of autonomic nervous system</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="divisions-of-adrenal-cortex">Divisions of adrenal cortex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#divisions-of-adrenal-cortex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Consists of three distinct layers</p>
<ol>
<li>Zona Glomerulosa – they secretes mineralocorticoids e.g. aldosterone. This is controlled by plasma concentration of angiotensin II</li>
<li>Zona Fasciculata – middle layer and widest. secreats Glucocorticoids e.g. cortisol, corticosterone. Controlled by hypothalamic-pituitary axis through ACTH</li>
<li>Zona Reticularis – the deep layer of the adrenal cortex, mainly secretes androgens</li>
</ol>
<p>Chapter 11 – Plate Form</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-35379603.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<p>cont</p>
<ol>
<li>ADRENAL CORTEX;</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>produces three steroid hormones</li>
<li>Glucocorticoids mainly cortisol or hydrocortisone</li>
<li>Mineralocorticoids mainly aldosterone</li>
<li>Sex hormones like testosterone (androgen)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-glucocorticoids-metabolic-effects-of-glucocorticoids">Functions of Glucocorticoids (metabolic effects of Glucocorticoids)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-glucocorticoids-metabolic-effects-of-glucocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Gluconeogenesis – formation of new sugars from non-sugars e.g proteins</li>
<li>Carbohydrate metabolism hence raising blood sugar (hyperglycemia)</li>
<li>Reduced cell utilization of glucose</li>
<li>Lipolysis; breakdown of triglycerides into fatty acids and glycerol for energy production</li>
<li>stimulate breakdown of proteins releasing amino acids which can be used for synthesis of other proteins</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-glucocorticoids">1.GLUCOCORTICOIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-glucocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cortisol or hydrocortisone is the main hormone</li>
<li>Its release is stimulated by ACTH from anterior pituitary gland</li>
<li>Secretion is controlled by negative feedback system</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glucocorticoids">Glucocorticoids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glucocorticoids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cortisol (very potent, accounts for about 95 percent of all glucocorticoid activity)</li>
<li>Corticosterone (provides about 4 per cent of total glucocorticoid activity)</li>
<li>Cortisone (synthetic, almost as potent as cortisol)</li>
<li>Prednisone (synthetic, four times as potent as cortisol)</li>
<li>Methylprednisone (synthetic, five times as potent as cortisol)</li>
<li>Dexamethasone (synthetic, 30 times as potent as cortisol)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physiological-and-pharmacological-effects">Physiological and pharmacological effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiological-and-pharmacological-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Anti-inflammatory actions</li>
<li>Suppression of immune responses</li>
<li>Delayed wound healing.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mineralocorticoids-aldosterone">MINERALOCORTICOIDS (ALDOSTERONE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mineralocorticoids-aldosterone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Secreted in Zona Glomerulosa</li>
<li>Main function is regulation of electrolytes concentration in extracellular fluids particularly sodium and potassium ions</li>
<li>This is by increasing uptake of sodium from the kidney nephrone.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrenal-medulla">ADRENAL MEDULLA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrenal-medulla" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Produces catecholamines: epinephrine and norepinephrine</li>
<li>Epinephrine is also called Adrenaline</li>
</ul>
<p>Its functions include;</p>
<ul>
<li>it increases contraction of the heart</li>
<li>causes bronchodilation of bronchial muscles</li>
<li>causes vasoconstriction of the blood vessels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-functions-of-catecholamines">General functions of catecholamines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-functions-of-catecholamines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stimulate the fight or fight reaction</li>
<li>Increased plasma glucoses levels</li>
<li>Increased cardiovascular function</li>
<li>Increased metabolic function</li>
<li>Decreased gastrointestinal and genitourinary function.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pancrease">PANCREASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pancrease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are three main types of cells found in pancreatic islet</li>
<li>Alpha cells : secrete glucagon</li>
<li>Beta cells : secrete insulin</li>
<li>Delta cells : secrete somatostatin.</li>
<li>Normal blood glucose levels is 5.5 -8.5 mmol/l</li>
<li>Blood glucose levels are control by opposing actions of insulin and glucagon</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin">INSULIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Its main function is to lower raised blood glucose levels</li>
<li>It lowers blood glucose levels by:
i. Acting on cell membrane and stimulating uptake and use of glucose by muscle and connective tissue cells
ii. Increasing conversion of glucose to glycogen (glycogenesis) for storage
iii. Signals the liver to stop releasing glucose
iv. Enhances storage of dietary fats in the adipose tissue</li>
<li>Secretion of insulin is stimulated by increased blood glucose levels e.g. after eating a meal.</li>
<li>It also inhibits glycogenolysis and gluconeogenesis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="glucagon">GLUCAGON<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glucagon" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Secretion is stimulated by low blood glucose levels and exercise</li>
<li>It promotes conversion of glycogen to glucose in liver and skeletal muscle (glycogenolysis)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-examination">Physical examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="and">And<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#and" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-taking">History taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-of-endocrine-dysfunction">ASSESSMENT OF ENDOCRINE DYSFUNCTION.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-of-endocrine-dysfunction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Consist of Health History, Physical Examination and lab and diagnostic studies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-health-history">1. Health History.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-health-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Elicit a description of client's present illness and chief complain including onset, course, location, precipitating and alleviating factors.</p>
<ul>
<li>Cardinal signs and symptoms indicating altered endocrine and metabolic function include:</li>
<li>☑ unexplained weight loss or gain</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Alteration in metabolic rate e.g. Tachycardia or bradycardia, diarrhoea or constipation.</li>
<li>Sleep pattern disturbances</li>
<li>Labile mood swings and change in mental status</li>
<li>Alteration in sexual performance</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Explore the client’s health history for risk factors associated with endocrine and metabolic disorders including</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Family history of endocrine disorders</li>
<li>☑ Radiation therapy and trauma</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-physical-examination">2. Physical examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Assess vital signs and measure body weight
b) Inspection</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe stature, fat distribution and shape of the face</li>
<li>Assess for the presence of goitre (enlarged thyroid gland)</li>
<li>Note protruding or sunken eyes and lid or retraction.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Note the color, texture and turgor of the skin, surgical scars and unusual bruising.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Palpation; palpate the thyroid for size, shape, symmetry and tenderness</p>
<p>d) Auscultation</p>
<ul>
<li>Auscultate heart, lung and bowel sounds</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-laboratory-and-diagnostic-studies">3. LABORATORY AND DIAGNOSTIC STUDIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-laboratory-and-diagnostic-studies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Measurement of hormones in the blood and urine</li>
<li>Reflects production and activity of hormones related to specific endocrine and metabolic disorders</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-laboratory-and-diagnostic-studies">3. LABORATORY AND DIAGNOSTIC STUDIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-laboratory-and-diagnostic-studies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-thyroid-function-tests-tfts">1. Thyroid function tests (TFTs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-thyroid-function-tests-tfts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Measurements of TSH, T3 and T4.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Normal serum levels of T3 70-220ng/dl..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Usually done to diagnose hypothyroidism and hyperthyroidism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elevated T3 and T4 with depressed TSH reflect primary hyperthyroidism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduced T3 and T4 with depressed TSH reflect primary hypothyroidism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the TSH level is <strong>high</strong> and the FT4 result is <strong>low</strong> this suggests an <strong>under-active thyroid</strong> (hypothyroidism) that requires treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the TSH level is <strong>low</strong> and the FT4 result is <strong>high</strong> this suggests an <strong>over-active thyroid</strong> (hyperthyroidism) that requires treatment.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-radioactive-iodine-uptake-test">2. Radioactive iodine uptake test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-radioactive-iodine-uptake-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A client take an oral dose of a small amount radioiodine</li>
<li>over time, the iodine collects in the thyroid because thyroid uses iodine</li>
<li>It is checked after 2, 6 or 24 hrs to determine how much iodine has been absorbed by thyroid</li>
<li>Increased uptake may indicate <strong>hyperfunctioning</strong> of thyroid gland</li>
<li>Decreased uptake may indicate <strong>hypofunctioning</strong> of the gland</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-thyroid-scan">3. Thyroid scan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-thyroid-scan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Performed to identify nodules or growth in the thyroid gland, tumors and growths in the brain.</li>
</ul>
<p>Before thyroid scan is taken:</p>
<ul>
<li>Client is put on NPO</li>
<li>Thyroid medications are temporarily withheld</li>
<li>After the test has been done, ensure proper disposal of waste.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-glucose-tolerance-test-gtt">4. Glucose Tolerance Test (GTT);<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-glucose-tolerance-test-gtt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sometimes it is called Oral Glucose Tolerance Tests (OGTT)</li>
<li>Glucose is given to patient</li>
<li>After 2 hrs, samples of blood are taken to determine how quickly it is cleared from the blood.</li>
<li>It is used to test for type 2 diabetes, insulin resistance and disorders of carbohydrate metabolism.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="before-test">Before test:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#before-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide high carbohydrate food for 3 days</li>
<li>Instruct client to avoid alcohol, smoking and caffeine.</li>
<li>Put the client on NPO for 10 hrs before the test.</li>
<li>After test, instruct the client to avoid any strenuous activity for 8 hrs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-glycosylated-hemoglobin-a-1c-hba1c">5.Glycosylated hemoglobin A-1C (HBA1C)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-glycosylated-hemoglobin-a-1c-hba1c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Refers to blood glucose bound to RBCs hemoglobin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to gauge how one is managing the Diabetes and to diagnose type one and type 2 DM.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It reflects average blood sugars for the last 2-3 months.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>HBA1C measures percentage of hemoglobin coated with sugar</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Normal HBA1C is 4%-5.6% for non-diabetic patient</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Levels at 5.7%-6.4% indicate high risk for diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Levels above 6.4% indicate diabetes</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-endocrine-system">DISORDERS OF ENDOCRINE SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetes-mellitus-dm">DIABETES MELLITUS (DM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetes-mellitus-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetes-mellitus">DIABETES MELLITUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetes-mellitus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a group of metabolic diseases characterized by elevated levels of glucose in the blood (hyperglycemia)</li>
<li>It results from defects in insulin secretion, insulin action or both.</li>
<li>Major sources of glucose in the body are:</li>
<li>☑ ingested food in the GIT</li>
<li>☑ formation of glucose by the liver</li>
<li>Insulin is a hormone produced by the pancreas</li>
<li>Beta cells in the islets of langerhans</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>It acts by: Regulating the blood production and storage of glucose</li>
<li>In diabetic state the cells may stop responding to insulin or the pancreas may stop producing insulin entirely</li>
<li>The WHO estimates that the prevalence of DM in Kenya at 2.7% (rural) to 10.7% (urban) KDMIC, 2012)</li>
<li>It is usually prevalent in the elderly with up to 50% of people older than 65 suffering some degree of glucose intolerance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Type 1 diabetes mellitus
b) Type 2 diabetes mellitus
c) Gestational diabetes
d) Diabetes due to other conditions and syndromes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="type-1-diabetes-mellitus">TYPE 1 DIABETES MELLITUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-1-diabetes-mellitus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The beta cells of pancreas no longer produce insulin due to destruction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Characterized by</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ hyperglycemia,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ breakdown of body fats and protein and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ development of ketosis (Condition associated with high level of ketone bodies in the body)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ketone bodies: acetone, acetoacetic acid, beta-hydroxybutyric acid, produced during the metabolism of fats.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Accounts for 5 – 10 % of cases of diabetes; most often occurs in childhood or adolescence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Formerly called Juvenile-onset diabetes or insulin-dependent diabetes (IDDM)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insulin administration is a must!!</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>ct</p>
<ul>
<li>Autoimmune destruction of beta cells arise either by genetic, immunologic or environmental factors</li>
<li>Immune mediated DM commonly develops during childhood and adolescence (juvenile onset) though it can occur at any age.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-type-1-diabetes">Pathophysiology of type 1 diabetes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-type-1-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There is autoimmune reaction in which the beta cells that produce insulin are destroyed.</li>
<li>Results in</li>
<li>☑ decreased insulin production,</li>
<li>☑ unchecked glucose production in the liver and</li>
<li>☑ fasting hyperglycemia.</li>
<li>☑ Alpha cells produce excess glucagon causing hyperglycemia</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Glucose derived from food fails to be stored in the liver</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It instead stays in the blood stream</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>contributes to postprandial (after meals) hyperglycemia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the concentration of glucose in the blood exceeds the renal threshold for glucose(9.9-11.1 mmol/L),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The kidneys may fail to reabsorb all of the filtered glucose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This leads to glucosuria...sweet urine what's that??</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When excess glucose is excreted in the urine it is accompanied by excessive loss of fluids and electrolytes (osmotic diuresis)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Due to shortage of glucose in the cells, the body resorts to breakdown of fats leading to formation of ketone bodies ... leads to ketoacidosis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Low PH</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors-for-type-1-diabetes">Risk factors for type 1 diabetes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-for-type-1-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetic predisposition for increased susceptibility; HLA susceptibility</li>
<li>Viral infections: eg German measles, coxsackie, and mumps.</li>
<li>Race/ethnicity</li>
<li>Geography as you move away from the equator</li>
<li>Family history: if a family member has (or had) type 1, you are at a higher risk.</li>
<li>Early diet:</li>
<li>Other autoimmune conditions:</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations-of-type-1-dm">Clinical manifestations of type 1 DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations-of-type-1-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Process of beta cell destruction occurs slowly</li>
<li>hyperglycemia occurs when 80 – 90% of beta cells are destroyed; often trigger stressor event (e.g. illness)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperglycemia-leads-to">Hyperglycemia leads to:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperglycemia-leads-to" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Polyuria (hyperglycemia acts as osmotic diuretic)</li>
<li>Glucosuria (Glucose in urine).</li>
<li>Polydipsia (thirst from dehydration from polyuria)</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Polyphagia (hunger and eats more since cell cannot utilize glucose)</li>
</ul>
<p>"A patient is starved in plenty"</p>
<ul>
<li>Weight loss (body breaking down fat and protein to restore energy source)</li>
<li>Malaise and fatigue (from decrease in energy)</li>
<li>Blurred vision (swelling of lenses from osmotic effects)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="type-2-diabetes-mellitus">Type 2 Diabetes mellitus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-2-diabetes-mellitus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition: condition of fasting hyperglycemia occurring despite availability of body's own insulin</li>
<li>Is the most common type of diabetes 90-95% of the cases</li>
<li>Was known as <strong>non-insulin dependent diabetes (NIDDM)</strong> or adult onset diabetes</li>
<li>occurs due to: Impaired insulin secretion and/or Insulin resistance</li>
<li>Insulin resistance refers to <strong>decrease tissue sensitivity to insulin</strong></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-type-2-dm">Pathophysiology of type 2 DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-type-2-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Type 2 DM occurs due to Impaired insulin secretion and Insulin resistance</li>
<li>To overcome insulin resistance and to prevent the build up of glucose in the blood, increased amounts of insulin are secreted to maintain normalcy</li>
<li>If beta cells fail to keep up with the increased demand for insulin, the glucose level rises and type 2 DM develops</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2ec19f21.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg">
Impaired insulin secretion
Pancreas</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b8623bef.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg">
Gastrointestinal absorption of glucose</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-8c3c3afe.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg">
Hyperglycemia
Liver
Increased basal hepatic glucose production</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-f812e39a.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg">
Muscle
Decreased insulin-stimulated glucose uptake</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors-for-type-2-dm">Risk factors for type 2 DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-for-type-2-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>History of diabetes in parents or siblings; no HLA</li>
<li>Obesity (especially of upper body)</li>
<li>Physical inactivity</li>
<li>Race/ethnicity: African American, Hispanic, or American Indian origin</li>
<li>Women: history of gestational diabetes,</li>
<li>Clients with hypertension; HDL cholesterol &lt; 35 mg/dL, and/or triglyceride level &gt; 250 mg/dL</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="manifestations-of-type-2-dm">Manifestations of type 2 DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#manifestations-of-type-2-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Most patients present with the classical symptoms of diabetes, including</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ polyuria,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ polydypsia and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ polyphagia (the 3P’s)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Additionally, some patients present with diabetic coma (hyperosmolar hyperglycemic non-ketotic states).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In type 2 DM there is enough insulin present to prevent the breakdown of fats hence ketone bodies are not present</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uncontrolled type 2 DM leads to Hyperglycemic hyper osmolar non ketotic syndrome (HHNKS)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gestational-diabetes">Gestational diabetes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gestational-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is any degree of glucose intolerance with its onset in pregnancy</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia develops in pregnancy because of secretion of placental hormones which causes insulin resistance</li>
<li>All pregnant women who meet the following criteria should be screened for DM:</li>
<li>Obese, age 25 years or older, age 25 year or younger and a history of DM in first degree relatives</li>
<li>It occurs in up to 14% of pregnant women and increases the risk for hypertensive disorders in pregnancies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>All types of diabetes have the 3P’s polyuria, polydipsia and polyphagia</li>
<li>Others, fatigue, weakness, vision changes, numbness in the hands or the feet, skin lession or wound that are slow to heal</li>
<li>Recurrent infection</li>
</ul>
