<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and diagnostic findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking</li>
<li>Physical examination: BP, BMI, neurologic exam etc</li>
<li>Lab finding</li>
<li>High fasting plasma glucose (6.0 mmol/L or more)</li>
<li>RBS of 11.1 mmol/L or more</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="history-taking">History taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diabetic history, both recent and historical</li>
<li>Symptoms of potential complications e.g. deterioration in eyesight</li>
<li>Drug history, current medications</li>
<li>Family history</li>
<li>Occupation and social history e.g. level of exercise, type of diet,</li>
<li>Smoking history, use of alcohol and recreational drugs</li>
<li>Prior knowledge of, attitudes to and concerns about the condition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examination">Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-examination">General examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Height/ weight/ BMI</li>
<li>Examination of feet (e.g. ulcers, loss of sensation)</li>
<li>Examination of eyes (e.g. cataracts, diabetic retinopathy)</li>
<li>Blood pressure measurement</li>
<li>Examination of peripheral pulses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-of-dm">DIAGNOSIS OF DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The diagnosis of diabetes must be confirmed biochemically prior to initiation of any therapy,</li>
<li>The presence of symptoms of hyperglycaemia, such as polyuria, polydypsia, lethargy, loss of weight and a random blood glucose (RBS) equal or above 11.1 mmol/L</li>
<li>Or a fasting capillary whole blood glucose &gt;6.1 mmol/L or more fasting blood sugar (FBS)</li>
<li>confirms the diagnosis of diabetes!</li>
<li>LOWER LIMIT for blood sugar is 3.3mmol/L</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-of-dm-in-asymptomatic-individuals">Diagnosis of dm in asymptomatic individuals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-dm-in-asymptomatic-individuals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In asymptomatic subjects a single abnormal blood glucose result is inadequate to make a diagnosis of diabetes.</li>
<li>The abnormal value must be confirmed at the earliest possible date using any of the following:
a) Fasting or random blood sample on two separate occasions or
b) a 75 g oral glucose tolerance test...</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">Aim:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To normalize insulin activity and blood glucose levels (euglycaemia) without hypoglycemia and without seriously disrupting the patient’s usual lifestyle and activity</li>
<li>To reduce development of vascular and neuropathic complications</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="components-of-dm-management">COMPONENTS OF DM MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-dm-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Pharmacologic therapy(Medical management)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional management</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Exercise</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>PHARMACOLOGIC THERAPY (MEDICAL MANAGEMENT)</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Consist of :-
a). oral glucose lowering agents
b). insulin therapy</p>
<p>a) Oral Glucose Lowering Agents (OGLAs)</p>
<ul>
<li>were previously referred to as oral hypoglycaemic agent</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications">Indications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Failure of lifestyle modifications</li>
<li>Fasting blood glucose level &gt; 11 mmol/L</li>
<li>Random blood glucose level &gt; 15 mmol/L.</li>
<li>When an individual's glycaemic targets are not met by the combination of dietary, modifications and physical activity/exercise.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classes-of-oral-hypoglycemic-agents">Classes of oral hypoglycemic agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classes-of-oral-hypoglycemic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Sulphonylureas</li>
<li>Biguanide</li>
<li>Thiazolidinediones</li>
<li>Meglitinides</li>
<li>Alpha_glucosidase inhibitors</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-sulphonyiureas">1. Sulphonyiureas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-sulphonyiureas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Action: Stimulates pancreatic cells to secrete more insulin and increases sensitivity of peripheral tissues to insulin</li>
<li>Used: to treat non-obese Type 2 diabetes</li>
<li>Example: Glibenclamide, Glipizide (Glucotrol), Chlorpropamide (Diabinese), Glimepiride : Gliclazide, Tolazamide (Tolinase)</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Glibenclamide</p>
<p>Starting Dose: 2.5 mg
Maximal dose: 15 mg
Major S/E: Hypoglycaemia* weight gain, skin rashes
C/I: Caution in liver and renal disease</p>
<p>b) Glipizide</p>
<p>Starting Dose: 5 mg
Maximal dose: 40 mg
Major S/E: Hypoglycaemia* weight gain, skin rashes
C/I: Caution in PG, liver and renal disease</p>
<p>c) Chlorpropamide: 250mg- 500mg</p>
<p>S/E : Hypoglycaemia* weight gain Skin rashes</p>
<p>C/I : Pregnancy, caution in liver and renal disease :</p>
<p>Others are</p>
<p>d) Glimepiride : 1mg-8mg</p>
<p>e) Gliclazide ; 40mg-320mg</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-biguanides">2. BIGUANIDES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-biguanides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Action: decreases overproduction of glucose by liver and makes insulin more effective in peripheral tissues</li>
<li>Used in obese diabetics</li>
<li>Does not stimulate insulin release</li>
<li>Metabolized by the kidney, do not use with renal patients</li>
<li>Example: Metformin (Glucophage)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Metformin : 500mg -2550mg</li>
<li>S/E : Abdominal pain, nausea, loose bowel motions lactic acidosis, increased flatulence</li>
<li>C/I : Renal, heart and liver failure;</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-meglitinides">3. Meglitinides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-meglitinides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Action: stimulates pancreatic cells to secret more insulin</li>
<li>Taken just before meals, rapid onset, limited duration of action</li>
<li>Major adverse effects is hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Used in non-obese diabetics</li>
<li>Example: Repaglinide (Prandin), Nateglinide (Starlix)</li>
</ul>
<p>Repaglinide : 1.0 mg -16mg</p>
<ul>
<li>S/E : Liver impairment, fluid retention, weight gain, anaemia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-thiazolidine-diones">4. THIAZOLIDINE DIONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-thiazolidine-diones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Action: Sensitizes peripheral tissues to insulin</li>
<li>Used in obese diabetics</li>
<li>Inhibits glucose production</li>
<li>Improves sensitivity to insulin in muscle, and fat tissue</li>
<li>Example: Rosiglitazone (Avandia), Pioglitazone (Actos)</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Rosiglitazone : 4mg - 8mg</p>
<p>S/E : Liver impairment, fluid retention weight gain, anaemia, hypotension, death, heart failure</p>
<p>C/I : Renal, heart and liver failure; cardiac disease class III and IV, pregnancy</p>
<p>b) Pioglitazone : 15mg - 45mg</p>
<p>S/E : Liver impairment, fluid retention weight gain, anaemia, Renal, heart and liver failure; pregnancy</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>ALPHA_GLUCOSIDASE INHIBATORS</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Action: Slow carbohydrate digestion and delay rate of glucose absorption</li>
<li>Take with first bite of the meal or 15 min. after</li>
<li>Adjunct to diet to decrease blood glucose levels</li>
</ul>
<p>Example: Acarbose (Precose), Miglitol (Glyset)</p>
<p>Acarbose: 25mg - 300mg</p>
<ul>
<li>S/E: Dyspepsia loose bowel motions, Flatulence</li>
</ul>
<p>PRECAUTIONS WHEN USING ORAL HYPOGLYCEMIC AGENTS</p>
<ul>
<li>If overweight (BMI &gt; 25 kg/m2) Metformin should be the first choice.</li>
<li>If Metformin is contraindicated, thiazolidinediones may be used</li>
<li>Long-acting sulphonylureas should be avoided in elderly patients.</li>
<li>In such patients, use short-acting sulphonylureas such as glimepiride, gliclazide</li>
</ul>
<p>CONT</p>
<ul>
<li>Metformin should be used with care in the elderly (over the age of 75 years) and is contraindicated in people with elevated serum creatinine, liver disease and severe respiratory, cardiac and peripheral vascular disease</li>
<li>Combination therapy using OGLAs with different mechanisms of action is indicated if monotherapy with one of the agents has failed.</li>
</ul>
<p>B) INSULIN THERAPY</p>
<ul>
<li>In type 1 diabetes, exogenous insulin is a must to be administered for life because the body looses ability to produce insulin.</li>
<li>In type 2 diabetes, insulin may be necessary on long term basis to control glucose levels if meal planning and oral agents are in effective.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin">Insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>10 ml</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-db2c689f.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications-of-insulin-therapy">Indications of insulin therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications-of-insulin-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) All type 1 diabetics since their bodies essentially no longer produce insulin</p>
<p>b) Some Type 2 diabetics, if oral medications are not adequate for control (both oral medications and insulin may be needed)</p>
<p>c) Diabetics enduring stressor situations such as surgery, corticosteroid therapy, infections, treatment for DKA, HHNKS</p>
<p>d) Women with gestational diabetes who are not adequately controlled with diet</p>
<p>cont</p>
<p>PREPARATIONS</p>
<ul>
<li>A number of insulin preparations are available</li>
<li>They vary according to their characteristics : time of course of action, sources or species and manufacturers.</li>
</ul>
<p>TIME COURSE OF ACTION</p>
<ul>
<li>Insulin may be grouped into four main categories based on onset, peak and duration of action.</li>
<li>They are:
Rapid acting, Short acting, intermediate and long acting insulin.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<p>a) Rapid acting insulins produce a more rapid effect that is of shorter duration.</p>
<ul>
<li>Because of rapid onset, the patient should be instructed to eat within 5 to 15 minutes after injection.</li>
<li>Due to short action period, the patient requires long acting insulin to maintain glucose control</li>
<li>Basal insulin is required to maintain glucose control</li>
<li>Intermediate-acting insulins function as basal insulins. Basal insulin works day and night to control blood sugar between meals and during sleep.</li>
<li>They keep blood glucose at a consistent levels during fasting</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<p>b) Short acting insulin are called regular insulin. Regular insulin is a CLEAR solution and is usually administered 20-30 minutes before meal. It is the only insulin approved for IV use.</p>
<p>c) Intermediate acting insulin are also called NPH (Neutral Protamine Hagedorn), they are similar in their time course of action, but appear WHITE AND CLOUDY</p>
<p>d) In long acting insulins, insulin is absorbed very slowly over 24hrs and can be given once a day.</p>
<p>Types of insulin and their properties</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Insulin preparation</th><th>Onset of action (hrs.)</th><th>Peak action</th><th>Duration of action (hrs.)</th><th>Injections per day</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Rapid-acting</td><td>10-20 min</td><td>1-2</td><td>3-5</td><td>Immediately before meals or with meals</td></tr><tr><td>Short acting</td><td>30-60 min</td><td>2-4</td><td>6-8</td><td>30 min before meals</td></tr><tr><td>Intermediate (NPH)</td><td>1-2h</td><td>5-7</td><td>13-18</td><td>Once or twice</td></tr><tr><td>Long acting</td><td>1-2 hours</td><td>peakless</td><td>24 h</td><td>Once</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulins-available-in-local-market">Insulins available in local market<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulins-available-in-local-market" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Insulin preparation</th><th>Examples available in the market</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Rapid-acting</td><td>Humalog or lispro, Novolog or aspart, Apidra or glulisine</td><td>Rapid-acting insulin covers insulin needs for meals eaten at the same time as the injection</td></tr><tr><td>Short Acting (soluble)</td><td>Regular (R) humulin or novolin, Velosulin (for use in the insulin pump)</td><td>Short-acting insulin covers insulin needs for meals eaten within 30-60 minutes</td></tr><tr><td>Intermediate</td><td>Humulin N (NPH (N)) Novolin N Lente</td><td>Intermediate-acting insulin covers insulin needs for about half the day or overnight.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>cont</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Biphasic mixture 30/70 Premixed insulin)*</th><th>Humulin 70/30, Novolog 70/30, Novolin 70/30</th><th>Twice a day before meal time</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Long acting</td><td>Lantus/Glargine Levemir/ Detemir Ultralente</td><td>Once a day</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-mixed-insulin">Pre-mixed insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-mixed-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pre-mixed insulin contain a combination of a rapid acting and intermediate acting insulin in fixed proportion.</li>
<li>This product eliminates difficult encountered while mixing two preparations of insulin</li>
<li>It indicated in ratios and first ratio indicate rapid or short acting while the second ratio indicate intermediate acting</li>
</ul>
<p>examples are : Humulin 70/30, Novolog 70/30, Novolin 70/30. are called biphasic mixtures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supplemental-insulin-therapy">Supplemental insulin therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supplemental-insulin-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Supplement oral hypoglycemic agents</li>
<li>Intermediate acting insulin is given at 10pm</li>
<li>Total Daily Dose calculated by: Kg x 0.2 IU of insulin (70 kg patient x 0.2 IU = 14 IU insulin).</li>
<li>The OGLAs are continued (half maximum dose of sulphonylureas and metformin dose of 2 g/day, or the sulphonylureas stopped and metformin continued).</li>
<li>Monitor blood glucose levels when possible.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="substitution-insulin-therapy">Substitution insulin therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substitution-insulin-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral hypoglycemic are discontinued .(unless the patient is obese where METFORMIN will be continued),</li>
<li>PRE-MIXED insulin is introduced twice daily at a dosage of 0.2 IU/kg body weight.</li>
<li>This is split into 2/3 in the morning and 1/3 in the evening, at 30 minutes before the morning and the evening meals.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="health-messages-shared-to-the-patient-discharged-with-mixtard">Health messages shared to the patient discharged with mixtard.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-messages-shared-to-the-patient-discharged-with-mixtard" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A patient discharge on mixtard to be used at home should be taught on the following</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of insulin syringes and how to withdraw the right dose.</li>
<li>How to administer through the right route</li>
<li>Sites of insulin administration, show the patient all sites in the body where insulin can be administered.</li>
<li>Teach the patient on signs and symptoms of hypoglycemia.</li>
<li>Teach the patient to carry sweeteners or glucose in case of hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Teach the patient on how to store insulin in cold place.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="human-mixtard">HUMAN MIXTARD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-mixtard" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>

</li>
<li>

</li>
<li>
<p>Human Mixtard contains Premixed Human Insulin. (30:70 &amp; 50:50)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>30% Regular Insulin &amp; 70% NPH Insulin.</p>
</li>

</li>

</li>

</li>

</li>

</li>
