<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-of-insulin-therapy">Complications of insulin therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-insulin-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Local allergic reaction characterised by redness, swelling, tenderness and indurations of 2-4 cm wheal may appear 1 to 2 hrs after insulin administration at the site of injection. Physician may prescribe antihistamine to be taken 1 hr before injection.</li>
<li>Systemic allergic reaction: are rare, but when they occur, there is immediate local skin reaction that gradually spreads into generalised urticaria (hives)</li>
<li>Treatment involves desensitization with small doses of insulin administered in gradually increasing amount using desensitization kit.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Insulin lipodystropy : loss of subcutaneous fat tissue that can occur as a result of repeated insulin injections at the same site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insulin resistance ; physiological condition in which cells of the body fails to respond to normal action of insulin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>clinically, it is defined as a daily insulin requirement of 200iu units or more. Immune antibodies develop and bind to the insulin, thereby decreasing insulin available for use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypoglycemia: most common complication due to delay in taking a meal or using too much insulin.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-includes">Signs and symptoms includes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Shakiness Nervousness or anxiety Sweating,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>chills and clamminess</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Irritability or impatience</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Confusion, including delirium</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rapid/fast heartbeat</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lightheadedness or dizziness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hunger and nausea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sleepiness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blurred/impaired vision</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tingling or numbness in the lips or tongue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Headaches</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weakness or fatigue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anger,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>stubbornness, or sadness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of coordination</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nightmares or crying out during sleep</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seizures Unconsciousness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All of the manifestations of hypoglycemia are rapidly relieved by glucose administration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If more severe hypoglycemia has produced unconsciousness or stupor, the treatment is 50 mL of 50% glucose solution by rapid intravenous infusion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is hypoglycemia without loss of consciousness, the patient can be given 15 or 20g of fast acting carbohydrate such as orange juice</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-nutritional-management">2. Nutritional management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-nutritional-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nutrition, diet and weight control are the foundation of DM management</li>
<li>The aim is to control the total caloric intake, to attain or maintain a reasonable body weight and control blood glucose levels (Greatly helps manage type 2 DM)</li>
</ul>
<p>GOALS:</p>
<ul>
<li>To provide all the essential food constituents necessary for optimal nutrition</li>
<li>To meet energy needs and maintain reasonable weight</li>
<li>Prevent wide fluctuations in blood glucose levels</li>
<li>To decrease serum lipid levels, if elevated and to reduce the risk of macro vascular disease</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caloric-requirements">Caloric requirements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caloric-requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Calorie controlled diets are planned by first calculating the individual energy needs and caloric requirements based on the patient’s age, gender, height and weight</li>
<li>An activity element is factored in to provide the actual number of calories required</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Currently caloric requirements are that the patients should take 0-60% carbohydrates, 20-30% from fat and 10-20% from protein</li>
<li>Recommendations regarding fat content is to reduce amount of saturated fats to 10% of total calories, limiting the total intake of cholesterol to less than 300mg/day</li>
<li>The meal plan for protein should include use of non animal sources of protein.</li>
<li>Use food guide pyramid to help patient with DM</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-dietary-management-of-type-2-diabetes-mellitus">Principles of dietary management of Type 2 diabetes mellitus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-dietary-management-of-type-2-diabetes-mellitus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pure (simple) sugars in foods and drinks should be avoided</li>
<li>At least three meals a day should be eaten, and binge eating should be avoided</li>
<li>Food quantities should be measured in volumes using available household items, such as cups, or be countable, such as number of fruits or slices of yam or bread.</li>
<li>Alcohol should be avoided.</li>
<li>Sweeteners are not essential and should be avoided as much as possible.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-exercise">3. EXERCISE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-exercise" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Exercise lowers the blood glucose level by increasing the uptake of glucose by body muscles and by improving insulin utilization</li>
<li>It also improves circulation and muscle tone</li>
<li>It also alters blood lipid levels, increasing the levels of high density lipoproteins and decreasing total cholesterol and triglyceride levels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-recommendations-for-exercise-in-dm">General recommendations for exercise in DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-recommendations-for-exercise-in-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Exercise at the same time, preferably when blood glucose levels are at their peak and the same amount each day</li>
<li>Regular exercise, rather than sporadic exercise should be encouraged</li>
<li>Use proper footwear and if appropriate other protective equipment</li>
<li>Avoid exercise in extreme heat or cold</li>
<li>Inspect feet daily after exercise</li>
<li>For patients older than 30 years and who have two or more risk factors for heart disease, an exercise stress test is essential</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The physical activity should be regular (-3 days/week), last at least 20-30 min. per session, and be of at least moderate activity</li>
<li>Activities like walking, climbing steps (instead of taking lifts) should be encouraged.</li>
<li>For sedentary persons with diabetes, a gradual introduction using a low-intensity activity like walking is mandatory.</li>
<li>Avoid strenuous exercise if ambient glycaemia is &gt;250 mg/dl (14 mmol/L), the patient has ketonuria or blood glucose is less than 8mg/dl (4.5mmol/L),</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="exercise-precautions-in-dm-patients">EXERCISE PRECAUTIONS IN DM PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exercise-precautions-in-dm-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Glycaemia (BLOOD SUGARS) should be monitored (using strips and meters) before and after planned strenuous physical activity as delayed hypoglycemia may occur.</li>
<li>Proper footwear must always be worn</li>
<li>Avoid strenuous exercise if ambient glycaemia is &gt; 250 mg/dl (14mmol/L), the patient has ketonuria or blood glucose is less than 80mg/dl (4.5mmol/l)</li>
<li>Avoid exercise in extreme heat or cold</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Monitoring blood sugars</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Important through self monitoring of blood glucose (SMBG)</li>
<li>Patients are instructed to keep a record or logbook of blood glucose levels so that they can detect patterns</li>
<li>Testing is done at the peak action time of medication to evaluate the need for dosage adjustments</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Diabetic education</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes education is the provision of knowledge and skill to people with diabetes that will empower them to render self-care in the management of their diabetes and associated disorders.</li>
</ul>
<p>HEALTH MESSAGES SHARED INCLUDE:</p>
<ul>
<li>What foods to eat, how much and how often to eat, how to exercise and its precautions, how and when to take medications</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>How to look after their feet, and thus prevent ulcers and amputations</li>
<li>How to avoid other long-term complications</li>
<li>That regular medical check ups are essential</li>
<li>When to seek medical help, e.g. How to identify hypoglycaemic and hyperglycaemic emergencies and symptoms, as well as signs of chronic complications</li>
<li>That diabetes is serious chronic disease, has no cure, but can be controlled</li>
</ul>
<p>Chart 41-7 • PATIENT EDUCATION</p>
<p>Self-Injection of Insulin</p>
<ol>
<li>With one hand, stabilize the skin by spreading it or pinching up a large area.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-bd904cf6.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
Pinching the skin</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Pick up syringe with the other hand and hold it as you would a pencil. Insert needle straight into the skin.*</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5c0c4759.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg">
Inserting the needle into the skin</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>To inject the insulin, push the plunger all the way in.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-069224be.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg">
Injecting the insulin</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Pull needle straight out of skin. Press cotton ball over injection site for several seconds.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-861c6e1d.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
Removing the needle and holding cotton ball over site</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Use disposable syringe only once and discard into hard plastic container (with a tight-fitting top) such as an empty bleach or detergent container.† Follow state regulations for disposal of syringes and needles.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-882f641f.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg">
Disposing of syringe</p>
<p>*Some patients may be taught to insert the needle at a 45-degree angle.</p>
<p>†Although some studies suggest that reusing disposable syringes may be safe, it is recommended that this be done only in the absence of poor personal hygiene, an acute concurrent illness, open wounds on the hands, or decreased resistance to infection.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-fd6a6297.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
GURE 41-7 Suggested areas for insulin injection.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-71e3c710.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management-of-a-patient-with-dm">NURSING MANAGEMENT OF A PATIENT WITH DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management-of-a-patient-with-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor fasting and random blood sugars daily and document the results in the cardex</li>
<li>Administer prescribed insulin, metformin and other sulphonylureas as prescribed in the treatment sheet.</li>
<li>Continuous monitoring of patient for signs of acute and chronic complications of diabetes.</li>
<li>Provide a balance diabetic diet that contain carbohydrates, protein, with less saturated fats.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to do physical activities like walking and climbing steps</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Initiate safety precautionary measures to prevent injury to the feet of the patient by providing foot wears.</li>
<li>Provide health education to the patient on recognition of signs and symptoms of hypoglycemia and hyperglycemia, exercises and kind of food to eat.</li>
<li>Monitor vitals signs to include BP, R, T, and pulse.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-complications-of-dm">Acute complications of DM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-complications-of-dm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are three major acute complications of DM related to short term imbalances in blood glucose levels</li>
</ul>
<p>They include :</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Diabetic ketoacidosis (DKA)</li>
<li>Hyperglycemic hyperosmolar non ketotic syndrome (HHNS)</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>HYPOGLYCEMIA</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Refers to low blood sugar</li>
<li>Occurs when the blood sugar falls below 3.3mmol/l</li>
<li>Occurs when insulin is at their peak levels</li>
<li>Severe hypoglycemia is a medical emergency</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSEs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To much insulin</li>
<li>Oral hypoglycemic agents</li>
<li>Excessive physical activity</li>
<li>Little food.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">CLINICAL MANIFESTATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>grouped into two categories:
a) adrenergic symptoms and
b) central nervous system (CNS) symptoms..</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In mild hypoglycemia, as the blood glucose level falls, the sympathetic nervous system is stimulated, resulting in a surge of epinephrine and norepinephrine.</li>
<li>This causes symptoms such as sweating, tremor, tachycardia, palpitation, nervousness and hunger.</li>
<li>In moderate hypoglycemia, the fall in blood glucose level deprives the brain cells of needed fuel for functioning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Signs of impaired function of the CNS may include inability to concentrate, headache, lightheadedness, confusion, memory lapses, numbness of the lips and tongue, slurred speech, impaired coordination, emotional changes, irrational or combative behavior, double vision and drowsiness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any combination of these symptoms (in addition to adrenergic symptoms) may occur with moderate hypoglycemia</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In severe hypoglycemia, CNS function is so impaired</li>
<li>Symptoms may include disoriented behavior, seizures, difficulty arousing from sleep, or loss of consciousness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-mild-hypoglycemia">Treatment for mild hypoglycemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-mild-hypoglycemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Immediate treatment: client should take 15 gm of rapid-acting sugar (half cup of fruit juice; glucose powder)
b) 15/15 rule: wait 15 minutes and monitor blood glucose; if still low, client should eat another 15 gm of sugar
c) Continue until blood glucose level has returned to normal</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-severe-hypoglycemia">Management of severe hypoglycemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-hypoglycemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) If client is conscious and alert, administer 5% or 10% dextrose infusion, if no dextrose, administer 15gm im glucagon
b) Monitor blood sugars until they become stable.
c) If client is unconscious, administer 10 mls of 50% bolus dextrose followed by 5% infusion
d) Monitor client response physically and also blood glucose level</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetic-ketoacidosis-dka">Diabetic ketoacidosis (DKA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetic-ketoacidosis-dka" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>DKA is caused by an absence or markedly inadequate amount of insulin.</li>
<li>It is a medical emergency</li>
<li>Results from breakdown of fat and overproduction of ketones by the liver and loss of bicarbonate</li>
<li>Common in type 1 DM but also type 2 are at risk</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Decreased or missed dose of insulin,</li>
<li>Illness or infection,</li>
<li>Undiagnosed and untreated diabetes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-precipitating-factors">Common Precipitating Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Include:</p>
<ul>
<li>UTI, URTI, gastroenteritis</li>
<li>Poor patient compliance with medication, or not increasing insulin when needed</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction, CVA</li>
<li>Thromboembolic disorders</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-dka">Pathophysiology of DKA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-dka" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Without insulin, the amount of glucose entering the cells is reduced and the liver :</li>
<li>Increases glucose production leading to hyperglycemia and</li>
<li>Breakdown of fat (lipolysis) into free fatty acids and glycerol leading formation of ketones</li>
<li>In an attempt to rid the body of the excess glucose, the kidneys excrete glucose along with water and electrolytes (eg, sodium and potassium) leading to osmotic diuresis.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>This osmotic diuresis, which is characterized by excessive urination (polyuria), leads to dehydration and marked electrolyte loss.</li>
<li>The Liver breakdown fat (lipolysis) into free fatty acids and glycerol. The free fatty acids are converted into ketone bodies by the liver</li>
<li>Ketone bodies are three product acetone, acetoacacetic acid and beta hydroxybutyric acid.</li>
<li>They are therefore acids; their accumulation in the circulation leads to metabolic acidosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestation-of-dka">Clinical manifestation of DKA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestation-of-dka" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The three main clinical features of DKA are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperglycemia</li>
<li>Dehydration and electrolyte loss</li>
<li>Acidosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="others-are">OTHERS ARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#others-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Kussmals respirations .deep urge to breath...air hunger</li>
<li>Deep breathing without labored breathing in an attempt to Blow off carbon dioxide to reverse acidosis</li>
<li>Fruity breath... Sweet breath</li>
<li>Nausea/ abdominal pain</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dehydration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lethargy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Coma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Polydipsia, polyuria, polyphagia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patients with marked intravascular volume depletion may have orthostatic hypotension (drop in systolic blood pressure of 20 mm Hg or more on standing).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Volume depletion may also lead to frank hypotension with a weak, rapid pulse.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-findings">Diagnostic findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Blood glucose levels may vary from 300 to 800 mg/dl (16.6 to 44.4 mmol/L).</li>
<li>Low serum bicarbonate (0 to 15 meq/l)</li>
<li>Low pH (6.8 to 7.3) values</li>
<li>Low PCO2 level (10 to 30 mm hg) reflects respiratory compensation (kussmaul respirations) for the metabolic acidosis.</li>
<li>Elevated levels of creatinine, blood urea nitrogen (bun)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="areas-of-focus-in-management-of-dka">AREAS OF FOCUS IN MANAGEMENT OF DKA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#areas-of-focus-in-management-of-dka" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Restoration of fluid balance</li>
<li>Correction of acidosis</li>
<li>Correction electrolyte imbalance</li>
</ol>
<p>Management involves</p>
<ul>
<li>Rehydration</li>
<li>Insulin injection</li>
<li>Monitoring of blood glucose, input and output, vital signs and arterial blood gases</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-management">Emergency management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Insulin is usually infused intravenously at a slow, continuous rate (eg, 5 units per hour).</li>
<li>Monitor blood glucose hourly</li>
<li>0.9% sodium chloride (normal saline) solution is administered at a rapid rate, usually 0.5 to 1 L per hour for 2 to 3 hours. Half-strength normal saline (0.45%) solution (also known as hypotonic saline solution) may be used for patients with hypertension or hypernatremia or those at risk for heart failure</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Monitoring fluid volume status and electrolytes levels and document the input and output</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs and arterial blood gases (including monitoring for orthostatic changes in blood pressure and heart rate), lung assessment.</li>
<li>Continuously assess the patient for the response to the ongoing treatment and for signs of hyperkalemia and document the findings</li>
</ol>
<p>NB : Bicarbonate infusion to correct severe acidosis is avoided during treatment of DKA because it precipitates further, sudden (and potentially fatal) decreases in serum potassium levels. :</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperglycemic-hyperosmolar-non-ketotic-syndrome-hhnks">HYPERGLYCEMIC HYPEROSMOLAR NON-KETOTIC SYNDROME (HHNKS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperglycemic-hyperosmolar-non-ketotic-syndrome-hhnks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Potential complication of type 2 diabetes that involves extremely high blood sugars without presence of ketones</li>
<li>In this condition, enough insulin is secreted to prevent ketosis, but not enough to prevent hyperglycemia</li>
<li>Life threatening medical emergency, high mortality rate, as high as 50% occurs</li>
<li>most often in older people (ages 50 to 70) with no known history of diabetes or with type 2 diabetes.</li>
<li>Hyperosmolarity is a condition in which has high conc. of salt, glucose and other substances that draws water out of other organs to blood stream.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precipitating-factors">Precipitating factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute illness (eg, pneumonia or stroke)</li>
<li>Medications that exacerbate hyperglycemia (thiazides)</li>
<li>Treatments, such as dialysis</li>
<li>The history includes days to weeks of polyuria with adequate fluid intake</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Altered level of consciousness (lethargy to coma)</li>
<li>Neurological deficits: motor and sensory impairment, seizures</li>
<li>Dehydration: dry skin and mucous membranes, extreme thirst, tachycardia, polyuria, hypotension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hyperglycemia leads to increased urine output and dehydration</li>
<li>Kidneys retain glucose; glucose and sodium rise</li>
<li>Severe hyperosmolar state develops leading to brain cell shrinkage</li>
<li>Diagnostic findings:</li>
<li>The blood glucose level is usually 600 to 1,200 mg/dL (33.33mmol/l - 66.66mmol/l)</li>
<li>Plasma osmolarity 340 mOsm/l or greater- normal 280-300mOsm/l</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-management">Emergency management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Similar to that of DKA: fluid replacement, correction of electrolyte imbalances, and insulin administration.</li>
<li>Patient is admitted to ICU and the following treatment initiated</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Insulin is usually administered at a continuous slow rate of 0.1 units/kg/hr to treat hyperglycemia</li>
</ol>
<p>Fluid treatment is started with</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>0.9% or 0.45% NS, depending on the patient's sodium level and the severity of volume depletion</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Potassium is added to IV fluids when urinary output is adequate and is guided by continuous electrocardiographic monitoring and frequent laboratory determinations of potassium.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Close monitoring of vital signs, fluid status, and laboratory values of electrolytes, blood gases and blood sugars.</li>
</ul>
<p>Comparison of Diabetic Ketoacidosis (DKA) and Hyperglycemic Hyperosmolar Nonketotic Syndrome (HHNS)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dka">DKA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dka" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Can occur in type 1 or type 2 diabetes; more common in type 1</li>
<li>Plasma bicarbonate level
&lt;15 mEq/L
Others????</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="long-term-complications">LONG TERM COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-term-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Chronic diabetic complications are grouped into three groups:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Macrovascular complications</li>
<li>Micro vascular complications, and</li>
<li>Neuropathies</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Micro vascular disease is due to damage to small blood vessels and macro vascular disease is due to damage to medium and large blood vessels.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic elevation of blood glucose level leads to damage of blood vessels (angiopathy).</li>
<li>The endothelial cells lining the blood vessels take in more glucose than normal, since they don't depend on insulin.</li>
<li>They then form more surface glycoproteins than normal, and cause the basement membrane to grow thicker and weaker</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="macrovascular-complications">MACROVASCULAR COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#macrovascular-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Result from changes in the medium to large blood vessels.</li>
<li>Blood vessel walls thicken, sclerose and become occluded by plaque that adheres to the vessel walls. Eventually, blood flow is blocked.</li>
<li>Coronary artery disease, cerebrovascular disease, and peripheral vascular disease are the three main types of macrovascular complications that occur more frequently in the diabetic population.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ecc1424d.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p>Plaque with fibrous cap</p>
<p>Cap ruptures</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-c76d5a3f.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ae367970.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p>Blood clot forms around the rupture, blocking the artery</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2ad232fc.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="microvascular-complications">MICROVASCULAR COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microvascular-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diabetic microvascular disease is characterized by capillary basement membrane thickening.</li>
<li>The basement membrane surrounds the endothelial cells of the capillary.</li>
<li>Micro-vascular complications include; Retinopathy, Nephropathy, neuropathy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetic-retinopathy">Diabetic retinopathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetic-retinopathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Growth of friable and poor-quality new blood vessels in the retina as well as macular edema (swelling of the macula), which can lead to severe vision loss or blindness.</li>
<li>Retinal damage makes it the most common cause of blindness among non-elderly adults</li>
<li>Characterised by Hemorrhage, swelling, decreased vision</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-development-of-retinopathy">Stages of development of retinopathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-development-of-retinopathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Background stage: asymptomatic retinopathy. Blood vessels within the retina develop microaneurysms that leak fluid, causing swelling and forming deposits (exudates)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pre-proliferative stage: Represents increased destruction of retinal blood vessels.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Proliferative stage: Abnormal growth of new blood vessels on the retina. New vessels rupture, bleeding into the vitreous humor and blockage of light.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-cb0e7109.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetic-nephropathy">Diabetic nephropathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetic-nephropathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: glomerular changes in kidneys of diabetics leading to impaired renal function</p>
<ul>
<li>First indicator: microalbuminuria</li>
<li>Diabetics without treatment go on to develop hypertension, edema, progressive renal insufficiency</li>
<li>In type 1 diabetics, 10 – 15 years</li>
<li>May occur soon after diagnosis with type 2 diabetes since many are undiagnosed for years</li>
<li>Most common cause of end-stage renal failure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetic-neuropathy">Diabetic Neuropathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetic-neuropathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diabetic neuropathy refers to a group of diseases that affect all types of nerves, including peripheral (sensorimotor), autonomic, and spinal nerves.</li>
<li>There is demyelinization of the nerves caused by hyperglycemia which disrupts conduction of impulses.</li>
<li>Common types of neuropathies are peripheral and autonomic neuropathies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-dysfunction">SEXUAL DYSFUNCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-dysfunction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Impotence (inability of the penis to become rigid and sustain an erection adequate for penetration) occurs with greater frequency in diabetic men than in nondiabetic men of the same age.</li>
<li>Some men with autonomic neuropathy have normal erectile function and can experience orgasm but do not ejaculate.</li>
<li>Retrograde ejaculation occurs: seminal fluid is propelled backward through the posterior urethra and into the urinary bladder</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetic-foot-problem">Diabetic foot problem<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetic-foot-problem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>People with diabetes are at increased risk of foot ulcers and amputations, which are major causes of morbidity and disability.</li>
</ul>
<p>Most common predisposing factors for ulcers and amputations are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Poor foot hygiene.</li>
<li>Unsuitable or no footwear</li>
<li>Peripheral vascular disease.</li>
<li>Peripheral neuropathy with loss of sensation</li>
<li>Deformities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cornerstones-of-management-of-foot-problems">Cornerstones of Management of Foot Problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cornerstones-of-management-of-foot-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Identification of the foot "at risk"</li>
<li>Regular inspection and examination of the foot at risk.</li>
<li>Education of health workers, people with diabetes and their families.</li>
<li>Appropriate footwear.</li>
<li>Early treatment of non-ulcerative and ulcerative problems</li>
</ul>
<p>How to reduce foot ulceration and amputations</p>
<ul>
<li>Optimize blood glucose, blood pressure and lipid control.</li>
<li>Ensure good nutrition status to promote healing.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to stop tobacco smoking/use.</li>
<li>Perform a detailed foot evaluation at presentation and annually.</li>
<li>People with demonstrated risk factors should be examined every 6 months.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examination-of-the-foot">Examination of the foot<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-foot" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>ASK FOR: Symptoms of neuropathy (numbness, tingling or pain) peripheral vascular disease (pain in calves on exercise and at rest)</li>
<li>EXAMINE SKIN: Inspect for ulcers, cracking, fragility, dryness, interdigital laceration and nail pathology</li>
<li>VASCULAR: Skin color, foot and ankle pulses</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>BONES/JOINTS: examine for deformities, e.g. claw toes and hammer toes.</li>
<li>FOOTWEAR: check footwear and socks both inside and outside</li>
<li>NEUROPATHY: check protective sensation using 10 g monofilament</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="somogyi-effect">Somogyi effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#somogyi-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Combination of hypoglycemia during night with a rebound morning hyperglycemia that may lead to insulin resistance for 12 to 48 hours</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-complication-of-diabetes">OTHER COMPLICATION OF DIABETES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-complication-of-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infections: patient become susceptible to infections.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d514aa88.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg"></p>
<p>CHANGINGlife
WITHDIABETES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="foot-care-for-people-with-diabetes">Foot Care for People with Diabetes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foot-care-for-people-with-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>People with diabetes have to take special care of their feet. You should have a comprehensive foot exam every year. This page shows some more things you can do to keep your feet healthy.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-038265b7.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<p>Wash your feet in warm water every day.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5cd2299c.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<p>Dry your feet well, especially between the toes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-033fdd31.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<p>Keep the skin soft with a moisturizing lotion, but do not apply it between the toes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d495a61e.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<p>Inspect your feet every day for cuts, bruises, blisters, or swelling. Tell your doctor right away if you find something wrong.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-f230e28b.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<p>Ask your diabetes care team how you should care for your toenails.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2121596a.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p>Wear clean, soft socks that fit you.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-c45905be.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<p>Keep your feet warm and dry. Always wear shoes that fit well.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-f42b0762.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg"></p>
<p>Never walk barefoot indoors or outdoors.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a24dcf7d.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg"></p>
<p>Examine your shoes every day for cracks, pebbles, nails, or anything that could hurt your feet.</p>
<p><strong>Take good care of your feet – and use them. A brisk walk every day is good for you.</strong></p>
<p>For more information, call the Novo Nordisk Diabetes Tip Line at 1-800-260-3730, or visit us online at ChangingDiabetes-us.com.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-4473b8f5.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg"></p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-areas-of-irritation-ulcers-diabetic-foot">Common areas of Irritation/Ulcers - Diabetic Foot<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-areas-of-irritation-ulcers-diabetic-foot" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-7a5bb002.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="somogyi-effect">Somogyi effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#somogyi-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Combination of hypoglycemia during night with a rebound morning hyperglycemia that may lead to insulin resistance for 12 to 48 hours</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-complication-of-diabetes">OTHER COMPLICATION OF DIABETES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-complication-of-diabetes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infections: patient become susceptible to infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pituitary-gland">PITUITARY GLAND<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pituitary-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders">DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pituitary-gland-disorders">PITUITARY GLAND DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pituitary-gland-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Abnormalities of pituitary function are caused by oversecretion or undersecretion of any of the hormones produced or released by the gland.</li>
<li>Oversecretion (hypersecretion) most commonly involves ACTH or growth hormone</li>
<li>Oversecretion of ACTH results in cushing’s syndrome</li>
<li>Oversecretion of growth results in acromegaly in adults :</li>
<li>acromegaly results in bone and soft tissue deformities and enlargement of the viscera without an increase in height.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Oversecretion of growth hormone in children results in gigantism</li>
<li>In insufficient secretion of growth hormone during childhood results in generalized limited growth and dwarfism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypopituitarism">HYPOPITUITARISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypopituitarism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Refers to hypofunctioning or hyposecretion of pituitary hormones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Result from disease of the pituitary gland itself or of the hypothalamus</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-hyposecretion-of-pituitary-hormones">Causes of hyposecretion of pituitary hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-hyposecretion-of-pituitary-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>radiation therapy to the head and neck area.</li>
<li>Trauma to the pituitary glands</li>
<li>Pituitary tumors</li>
<li>Vascular lesion in the pituitary gland</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperpituitarism">Hyperpituitarism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperpituitarism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Results in excess production and secretion of one or more hormones such as GH, PRL, ACTH.</li>
<li>Most common cause is a benign adenoma</li>
<li>Anterior pituitary adenoma,</li>
<li>a benign tumor.</li>
<li>Prolactin and GH are the hormones most commonly over-produced by adenomas.</li>
</ul>
<p>The Pituitary &amp; Hypothalamus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="changes-in-neurological-function-may-occur-as-adenomas-compress-surrounding-tissue">Changes in neurological function may occur as adenomas compress surrounding tissue.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changes-in-neurological-function-may-occur-as-adenomas-compress-surrounding-tissue" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Manifestations include headaches, visual defects and increased ICP (intracranial pressure)</p>
<p>Treatment is surgical resection through</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-0dfb233b.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-83c0ae4d.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="increased-gh">Increased GH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#increased-gh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased GH: <strong>Gigantism &amp; Acromegaly</strong></li>
<li>a statue of Robert Wadlow, the "Alton Giant," who measured 8 feet 11 inches at the time of his death.</li>
<li>Young 12 y/o male standing with his mother</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2c154d9e.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-c49dff32.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Gigantism is the result of GH hypersecretion before the closure of the epiphyseal plates (childhood).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abnormally tall but body proportions are normal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acromegaly is over secretion of GH in adulthood</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continued growth of boney, connective tissue leads to disproportionate enlargement of tissue..</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-26589528.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acromegaly">Acromegaly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acromegaly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rare condition – develops between ages 30-50</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Coarsening of facial features</li>
<li>Enlarged hands &amp; feet</li>
<li>Carpel trunnel syndrome</li>
<li>Excessive sweating &amp; oily skin</li>
<li>Headaches</li>
<li>Vision disturbance</li>
<li>Sleep apnea</li>
<li>General tiredness</li>
<li>Oligomenorrhea or amenorrhea</li>
<li>Impotence (adult males)</li>
<li>Decreased libido</li>
</ul>

<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-f9f83575.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<p>ADAM</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>History &amp; physical exam</li>
<li>Investigation includes:</li>
<li>GH analysis (glucose tolerance) Normally GH concentration falls with oral glucose; in acromegaly it does not.</li>
<li>Prolactin levels as well as other pituitary function tests</li>
<li>MRI or CT &amp; visual field tests to determine size and position of the adenoma.</li>
<li>Bone scan</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgery (primary choice)</li>
<li>Radiotherapy</li>
<li>Drug treatment – when surgery is not feasible</li>
<li>Combinations of above</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-treatment-of-acromegaly">Drug treatment of Acromegaly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-treatment-of-acromegaly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dopamine agonists: Dopamine agonists work to inhibit GH release from the tumour</li>
<li>Somatostatin: growth hormone receptor antagonist decreases the action of GH on target tissues</li>
<li>Dopamine agonists are taken by mouth but in generally are less effective than somatostatin analogues, which have to be injected.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anterior-pituitary-disorders">Anterior Pituitary Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anterior-pituitary-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Hormone</th><th>Increased level</th><th>Decreased level</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>GH</td><td>Gigantism (child)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Acromegaly (adult)</td><td>Dwarfism (child)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Lethargy, premature aging</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>ACTH</td><td>Cushing’s Disease</td><td>Addison’s Disease</td></tr><tr><td>TSH</td><td>Goiter, increased BMR, HR, BP</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Graves disease</td><td>Decreased BMR, HR, CO, BP</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Cretinism (children)</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Prolactin</td><td>amenorrhea</td><td>Too little milk</td></tr><tr><td>FSH</td><td></td><td>Late puberty, infertility</td></tr><tr><td>LH</td><td>Menstrual cycle disturbance</td><td>Amenorrhea, impotence</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="posterior-pituitary-disorders">Posterior Pituitary Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#posterior-pituitary-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Hormone</th><th>Increased</th><th>Decreased</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Oxytocin</td><td>Precipitates childbirth, excess milk</td><td>Prolonged childbirth, diminished milk</td></tr><tr><td>ADH (vassopressin)</td><td>Increased BP, decreased urinary output, edema. SIADH</td><td>Diabetes insipidus, dilute urine &amp; increased urine output</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dac08bb">Hyper – Posterior Pituitary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dac08bb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="siadh">SIADH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#siadh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Syndrome of Inappropriate Anti-Diuretic Hormone</li>
<li>Too much ADH produced or secreted.</li>
<li>SIADH commonly results from malignancies, CHF, &amp; CVA - resulting in damage to the hypothalamus or pituitary which causes failure of the feedback loop that regulates ADH.</li>
<li>Client retains water causing dilutional hyponaetremia &amp; decreased osmolality.</li>
<li>Decreased serum osmolality cause water to move into cells</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Lethargy &amp; weakness</li>
<li>Confusion or changes in neurological status</li>
<li>Cerebral edema</li>
<li>Muscle cramps</li>
<li>Decreased urine output</li>
<li>Weight gain without edema</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Serum sodium low</li>
<li>Serum osmolality low</li>
<li>Urine osmolality disproportionately elevated in relation to the serum osmolality</li>
