<li>Urine specific gravity elevated</li>
<li>Plasma ADH elevated</li>
</ul>
<p>Water intoxication, cerebral edema, severe hyponatremia cause altered neurological status, which untreated may cause death</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3c30bde7.jpeg" alt="img-47.jpeg"></p>
<p>!!!!!!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-of-siadh">Treatment of SIADH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-siadh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Treat underlying cause</li>
<li>Hypertonic or isotonic IV solution</li>
<li>Monitor for signs of fluid and electrolyte imbalance</li>
<li>Monitor for neurological effects</li>
<li>Monitor in and out</li>
<li>Weigh</li>
<li>Restrict fluid intake</li>
<li>Medic Alert</li>
<li>Lithium inhibits action of ADH to promote water excretion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2d975d7c">Hypofunction – Posterior pituitary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2d975d7c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="normal-urine-production">Normal urine production<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#normal-urine-production" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a5eeb768.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetes-insipitus-di">Diabetes Insipitus (DI)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetes-insipitus-di" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>DI is usually insidious but can occur with damage to the hypothalamus or the pituitary. (neurogenic DI)</li>
<li>May be a result of defect in renal tubules, do not respond to ADH (nephrogenic DI)</li>
<li>Decreased production or release of ADH results in massive water loss</li>
<li>Leads to hypovolemic &amp; dehydration</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-99d9de02.jpeg" alt="img-49.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-tests">Diagnostic Tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Serum sodium</li>
<li>Urine specific gravity</li>
<li>Serum osmolality</li>
<li>Urine osmolality</li>
<li>Serum ADH levels</li>
<li>Vasopressin test and water deprivation test: increased hyperosmolality is diagnostic for DI.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medical management includes</li>
<li>Rehydration IV fluids (hypotonic)</li>
<li>Symptom management</li>
<li>ADH replacement (vasopressin)</li>
<li>For nephrogenic DI: thiazide diuretics, mild salt depletion, prostaglandin inhibitors (i.e. ibuprophen)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing">Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Monitor for signs of fluid and electrolyte imbalance</li>
<li>Monitor in and out</li>
<li>Daily weight</li>
<li>Monitor for excessive thirst or output</li>
<li>Assess serum and urine values (decreased SG, decreased urine osmolality, high serum osmolality are early indicators)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="possible-nursing-diagnosis">POSSIBLE NURSING DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possible-nursing-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fluid Volume Deficit</li>
<li>Risk for Injury r/t altered LOC</li>
<li>Risk for Altered Health Maintenance</li>
<li>Sleep Pattern Disturbance r/t urinary frequency or anxiety</li>
<li>Altered Urinary Elimination r/t excess urinary output</li>
<li>Body Image</li>
<li>Altered sexuality</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="panhypopituitarism">Panhypopituitarism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#panhypopituitarism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When both the anterior and posterior fail to secrete hormones, the condition is called panhypopituitarism.</li>
<li>Causes include tumors, infection, injury, iatrogenic (radiation, surgery), infarction</li>
<li>Manifestations don’t occur until 75% of pituitary has been obliterated.</li>
<li>Treatment involves removal of cause and hormone replacement (adrenocortical insufficiency, thyroid hormone, sex hormones)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-thyroid-gland">DISORDERS OF THYROID GLAND<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-thyroid-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>HYPOTHYROIDISM</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypothyroidism">HYPOTHYROIDISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Def: refers to hyposecretion of thyroid hormones specifically T3 and T4.</li>
<li>It is also referred to as thyroid deficiency. Thyroid deficiency affect all body functions</li>
<li>When thyroid deficiency is present at birth, the condition is known as cretinism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Autoimmune thyroiditis (Hashimoto’s disease), in which the immune system attacks the thyroid gland.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It is the most common cause.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Atrophy of thyroid gland with aging</li>
<li>Radioactive iodine</li>
<li>Thyroidectomy</li>
<li>Medications like Lithium and Antithyroid medications</li>
<li>Radiation to head and neck for treatment of head and neck</li>
<li>cancers, lymphoma</li>
<li>Infiltrative diseases of the thyroid (amyloidosis, scleroderma)</li>
<li>Iodine deficiency and iodine excess</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">PREDISPOSING FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Previous treatment with antithyroid medications and radioactive iodine</li>
<li>Thyroidectomy</li>
<li>Advance age; common in older women</li>
<li>Radiation therapy for head and neck for cancer</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">PATHOPHYSIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypothyroidism can be caused by thyroid dysfunction itself or pituitary gland and hypothalamus.</li>
<li>In both, there is hyposecretion of T3 and T4 hormones which leads to decreased basal metabolic rate characterized by lethargy, fatigue, cold intolerance, weight gain and constipation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Extreme fatigue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>hair loss, brittle nails, and dry skin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>numbness and tingling of the Fingers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cold intolerance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight gain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>constipation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Forgetfullness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Menstrual disturbances such as menorrhagia or amenorrhea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Slowness of movement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bradycardia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>irritability</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hormone replacement therapy: synthetic levothyroxine is administered.</li>
<li>BRAND NAME: Synthroid, levoxyl, levothroid and unithroid</li>
<li>Is a drug of choice for most patients who need thyroid hormone replacement.</li>
</ul>
<p>MODE OF ACTION: It increases metabolic rate of all cells of all tissues in the body</p>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacokinetics">PHARMACOKINETICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacokinetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Most of it converted into T3 in the body hence can produce both T3 and T4</li>
<li>highly bound to proteins and has a half life of 7 days hence it therapeutic effects are delayed for 2 weeks</li>
<li>The long half life facilitate once a day dosing</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="therapeutic-uses-indications">THERAPEUTIC USES (INDICATIONS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-uses-indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Indicated in hypothyroidism in adult and children</li>
<li>Maintenance of thyroid hormones following surgery</li>
<li>Myxedema coma</li>
<li>Simple goiter.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dosage-and-administration">Dosage and administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage-and-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Starting dosage is 12.5mcg/day orally.</li>
<li>Dosage changes may differ with individual patients based upon age, the presence of cardiovascular disease and development of tolerance or reduced effectiveness of drug</li>
<li>The drug is available in tablet forms, capsules and IV.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions">Drug interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Increases the need of insulin in diabetic patients</li>
<li>Increases the effects of warfarin therefore monitoring of blood clotting is necessary</li>
<li>Increases cardiac response to catecholamines (epinephrine) thereby increasing the risk of catecholamine induced dysrhythmias.</li>
<li>Caution must be exercised when administering catecholamines to patients using the drug</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="duration-of-therapy">DURATION OF THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duration-of-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Replacement therapy must be continued for life.</li>
<li>The patient must be made fully aware of the chronic nature of the condition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management-of-hypothyroidism">Nursing management of hypothyroidism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management-of-hypothyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Promote independence in self-care
Activities by:
a. Spacing activities to promote rest and exercise as tolerated.
b. Assisting with self-care activities when patient is fatigued.
c. Monitor patient’s response to increasing activities.</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Provide extra layer of clothing or extra blanket to minimize heat loss</li>
<li>Avoid and discourage use of external heat source (eg, heating pads, electric or warming blankets). It reduces the risk of peripheral vasodilation and vascular collapse</li>
<li>Encourage increased fluid intake within limits of fluid restriction. It promotes passage of soft stool</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Administer hormone replacement: usually Levothyroxine(Synthroid)-should be taken on an empty stomach 30-60 min before eating...in the morning... food, iron and calcium..may reduce its absorption in the gut.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide foods with low calories and high in fiber. It increases bulk of stools and more frequent bowel movements.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor patient's vitals signs esp body temperature and report decreases from patient's baseline value.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Monitoring detects decreased body temperature and onset of myxedema coma baseline value.</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Health education : Explain rationale for thyroid hormone replacement</li>
<li>Advise to report palpitation, tachycardia, and chest pain when using levothyroxine</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="myxedema">MYXEDEMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myxedema" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Def: myxedema refers to the accumulation of mucopolysaccharides in subcutaneous and other interstitial tissues. There is thickening of skin with non pitting edema</li>
<li>Occurs in long-standing hypothyroidism. The term is used appropriately only to describe the extreme symptoms of severe hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>It presents with symptoms of hypothyroidism plus extreme hypothermia with personality and cognitive changes characteristic of dementia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hormone replacement therapy using levothyroxine</li>
<li>Treatment the underlying cause of hypothyroidism</li>
<li>Nursing management same as those of hypothyroidism</li>
<li>The patient is sensitive to sedatives, opioids, and anesthetic agents. Therefore, these medications are administered only with extreme caution.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="myxedema-coma">Myxedema coma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myxedema-coma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Myxedema coma describes the most extreme, severe stage of hypothyroidism, in which the patient is hypothermic and unconscious.</li>
<li>It is a life threatening condition and it is regarded as a medical emergency.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presenting-features">PRESENTING FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presenting-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Severe hypothermia</li>
<li>Depressed respirations</li>
<li>Coma</li>
<li>Cool clummy skin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-management">Emergency management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit the patient into the ICU</li>
<li>IV levothyroxine is administered until consciousness is restored. The patient is then continued on oral thyroid hormone therapy</li>
<li>Arterial blood gases are measured to determine CO2 retention and to guide the use of assisted ventilation to combat hypoventilation</li>
<li>Provide warmth to the patient by covering with enough blankets</li>
<li>Fluids are administered cautiously because of the danger of water intoxication</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="caution-when-administering-iv-levothyroxine-in-myxedema-coma">Caution when administering iv levothyroxine in myxedema coma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution-when-administering-iv-levothyroxine-in-myxedema-coma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>monitor for myocardial ischemia or infarction, which may occur in response to therapy</li>
<li>The nurse must also be alert for signs of angina, especially during the early phase of treatment; if detected, it must be reported and treated at once to avoid a fatal myocardial infarction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Administer prescribed medications (eg, levothyroxine) with extreme caution because the slow metabolism and atherosclerosis of Myxedema may result in angina with administration of levothyroxine</li>
<li>Assist in Ventilatory support: is necessary to maintain adequate oxygenation and maintenance of an airway.</li>
<li>Turn and reposition patient at interval. Minimizes risks associated with immobility</li>
<li>Monitor patients respiratory status.</li>
<li>Apply other nursing interventions of hypothyroidism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levothyroxine">Levothyroxine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levothyroxine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>50 micrograms Tablets
Levothyroxine Sodium</p>
<p>28 Tablets</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-404dff84.jpeg" alt="img-50.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperthyroidism">HYPERTHYROIDISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperthyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Def: Hyperthyroid state characterized by increased circulating T3 and T4</li>
<li>There is oversecretion of thyroid hormones by the thyroid gland.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevalence">PREVALENCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevalence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It affects women eight times more frequently than men, with onset usually between the second and fourth decades</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Overstimulation of thyroid gland by immunoglobulins</li>
<li>Thyroiditis</li>
<li>Excessive ingestion of thyroid hormone.</li>
<li>Tumors of thyroid gland or pituitary gland</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="forms-of-hyperthyroidism">FORMS OF HYPERTHYROIDISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forms-of-hyperthyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Graves disease: the most common type of hyperthyroidism, results from an excessive output of thyroid hormones caused by abnormal stimulation of the thyroid gland by circulating immunoglobulins.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Also called Toxic goiters: causes overstimulation of thyroid gland.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hyperthyroidism may occur with the release of excessive amounts of thyroid hormone as a result of inflammation after irradiation of the thyroid or destruction of thyroid tissue by tumor.</li>
<li>Excessive hormones leads to increased hormone activity which leads to increased Basal Metabolism and cardiac activity</li>
<li>Increased metabolism is characterised by increased appetite and dietary intake, progressive weight loss, abnormal muscular fatigability and weakness</li>
<li>The patients exhibits a group of sign and symptoms (sometimes called thyrotoxicosis)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>HEAT intolerance</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Tachycardia and palpitations and increased pulse pressure</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fast Pulse rate btw 90-160</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Exophthalmos (bulging eyes) with startled facial expression</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diarrhea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>flushed skin : warm, soft, and moist</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oligomenorrhea to amenorrhea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fine tremors and nervousness and clubbing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Irritability, mood swings, personality changes and agitation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Enlarged thyroid</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Osteoporosis and fractures</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hyperthyroidism">HYPERTHYROIDISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hyperthyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6729ca2f.jpeg" alt="img-51.jpeg"></p>
<p>©2007 Nursing Education Consultants, Inc.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead></table>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3b9e241b.jpeg" alt="img-52.jpeg">
A</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-16424569.jpeg" alt="img-53.jpeg">
B</p>
<p>Assessment findings</p>
<ul>
<li>Client has heat intolerance and may have diaphoresis (increased sweating) even when environmental temperatures are comfortable for others.</li>
<li>Client report palpitations or chest pain</li>
<li>Client experiences emotional lability ( mood instability ), irritability, decreased attention span and manic behaviour.</li>
<li>Fatigue, weakness and insomnia</li>
<li>The thyroid gland invariably is enlarged to some extent. It is soft and may pulsate</li>
<li>Increased serum levels of T4 and iodine intake by the thyroid gland</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Can be managed by:</p>
<ol>
<li>Pharmacological therapy</li>
<li>Surgical therapy</li>
</ol>
<p>PHARMACOLOGICAL THERAPY</p>
<p>(1) use of irradiation by administration of the radioisotope 121I or 131I for destructive effects on the thyroid gland
(2) antithyroid medications that interfere with the synthesis of thyroid hormones</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antithyroid-medications">Antithyroid medications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antithyroid-medications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Include ; propylthiouracil , carbimazole.</p>
<ol>
<li>PROPYLTHIOURACIL propacil( PTU)</li>
</ol>
<p>(A) Mechanism of action : inhibit thyroid hormone synthesis by inhibiting incorporation of iodine into tyrosine. It also suppress conversion of T4 into T3 the more active form of thyroid hormone.</p>
<p>(B) Pharmacokinetics</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>is rapidly absorbed following oral administration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Therapeutic effects begin after 30 mins</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The plasma half-life is short(2hrs).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>As a result ,it is administered three times a day</p>
<p>cont</p>
<p>(c) therapeutic uses /indications</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperthyroidism</li>
<li>Adjunct to radiation therapy. Used to control hyperthyroidism until effects of radiation become manifest.</li>
<li>Thyrotoxic crisis, (thyroid storm)</li>
</ul>
<p>(d) ADVERSE EFFECTS</p>
<ol>
<li>hypothyroidism; excessive dosing with PTU may lead to hypothyroidism</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>agranulocytosis; severe bone marrow depression. Resulting in failure to produce neutrophils. Usually occurs during the first 2 months of life. sore throat and fever are the earliest indications. Patients are instructed to report these immediately. The drug is stopped immediately if the symptom S/E develops.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>skin rashes, headaches, nausea and joint pains</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<p>DOSAGE : Propylthiouracil-100-150mg every 6 or 8 hrs</p>
<p>DURATION : 18-24 months</p>
<p><strong>PTU AND PREGNANCY</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>PTU crosses placenta</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Propylthiouracil is preferred over carbimazole in pregnant women because its rapid action reduces transfer across the placental barrier and it doesn't cause aplasia cutis (a severe skin disorder) in the fetus</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Mothers taking these drugs shouldn’t breast-feed.</li>
<li>If a breast-feeding woman must take one of these drugs, propylthiouracil is the preferred drug.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carbimazole">CARBIMAZOLE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carbimazole" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mechanism of action: decreases uptake iodine needed in formation of thyroxine and incorporation of iodine into tyrosine to form thyroxine</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dosage">Dosage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The initial dose is 15-40 mg daily given for 4 to 8 weeks until euthyroid status is achieved.</li>
<li>The dose is gradually reduced to a maintenance of 5-15 mg daily.</li>
<li>Treatment is usually required for 12-18 months</li>
<li>Patients should have their T4 levels checked every 4-6 weeks</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Once maintenance dose has been established, T4 and TSH should be checked every 3 months.</li>
<li>Patients should be regularly reviewed during the first year after discontinuing carbimazole because there is high rate of relapse during this period.</li>
<li>Carbimazole is used at the lowest dose possible in pregnancy however PTU is preferred over carbimazole</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="radioactive-iodine-therapy">Radioactive iodine therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radioactive-iodine-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Is used as a radiation therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to destroy thyroid tissue in patients with hyperthyroidism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mechanism of action: produce emission of beta particles that destroy thyroid tissue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduction of thyroid tissue is gradual and effects takes weeks to become apparent</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A single oral dose of the agent is administered</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is used as a radiation therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to destroy thyroid tissue in patients with hyperthyroidism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mechanism of action: produce emission of beta particles that destroy thyroid tissue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduction of thyroid tissue is gradual and effects takes weeks to become apparent</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Almost all the iodine that enters and is retained in the body becomes concentrated in the thyroid gland.</li>
<li>Radioactive isotope of iodine is concentrated in the thyroid gland, where it destroys thyroid cells without jeopardizing other radiosensitive tissues.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Antithyroid medications are contraindicated in late pregnancy because they may produce goiter and cretinism in the fetus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adjunctive-therapy">Adjunctive Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adjunctive-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Beta-adrenergic blocking agents are important in controlling the sympathetic nervous system effects of hyperthyroidism.</li>
<li>Propranolol (Inderal) is used to control nervousness, tachycardia, tremor, anxiety and heat intolerance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Provide adequate rest periods in a quiet room because fatigue is common</li>
<li>Administer anti-thyroid medications that block hormone synthesis- carbimazole and PTU and monitor for side effects</li>
<li>Provide a high-calorie diet, high protein to provide energy and build the body</li>
<li>Provide a cool and quiet environment to reduce irritability. Noises, such as loud music, conversation, and equipment alarms, are minimized.</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Maintain the environment at a cool, comfortable temperature and change beddings and clothing as needed. Cool baths and cool or cold fluids may provide relief.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assesses and monitor the patient's cardiac status, including heart rate, blood pressure, heart sounds, and peripheral pulses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To reduce diarrhea, highly seasoned foods and stimulants such as coffee, tea, cola, and alcohol are discouraged. In addition, fluids are added as needed</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thyroid-storm-thyrotoxic-crisis-thyrotoxicosis">Thyroid Storm (Thyrotoxic Crisis, Thyrotoxicosis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroid-storm-thyrotoxic-crisis-thyrotoxicosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An acute LIFE-threatening condition characterized by excessive thyroid hormone</li>
<li>Is the most severe form of hyperthyroidism with acute onset.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Thyroid storm is characterized by:</p>
<ol>
<li>High fever (hyperpyrexia) above 38.5°C (101.3°F)</li>
<li>Extreme tachycardia (more than 130 beats/min)</li>
<li>Severe weight loss, diarrhea, abdominal pain</li>
<li>dyspnea</li>
<li>Altered neurologic or mental state, which frequently appears as delirium, psychosis, or coma</li>
<li>Restlessness, Agitation, confusion and Seizures</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precipitating-factors">Precipitating factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Injury on the body</li>
<li>Systemic infection</li>
<li>Thyroid and non thyroid surgery</li>
<li>Tooth extraction</li>
<li>Insulin reaction</li>
<li>Diabetic acidosis</li>
<li>Pregnancy</li>
<li>Digitalis intoxication,</li>
<li>abrupt withdrawal of antithyroid medications,</li>
<li>Extreme emotional stress</li>
<li>Vigorous palpation of the thyroid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-management">EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Humidified oxygen is administered to improve tissue oxygenation and meet the high metabolic demands</li>
<li>Arterial blood gas levels or pulse oximetry may be used to monitor respiratory status.</li>
<li>Intravenous fluids containing dextrose are administered to replace liver glycogen stores that have been decreased in the hyperthyroid patient.</li>
<li>PTU or Carbimazole is administered to impede formation of thyroid hormone and block conversion of T4 to T3, the more active form of thyroid hormone.</li>
<li>Hydrocortisone is prescribed to treat shock or adrenal insufficiency.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Cool environment and acetaminophen (Tylenol) to reduce fever. Salicylates (eg, aspirin) are not used because they displace thyroid hormone from binding proteins and worsen the hypermetabolism</li>
<li>Propranolol, combined with digitalis, are administered to reduce severe cardiac symptoms</li>
<li>Iodine is administered to decrease output of T4 from the thyroid gland</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Maintain PATENT airway and adequate ventilation. Oxygen is needed to meet metabolic demands</li>
<li>Administer anti-thyroid drugs with medications such as
(a) Lugol's solution: consist of 5% Iodide and 10% potassium... blocks peripheral conversion of T4 to T3 hence inhibiting hormone release.
(b) Propranolol: is a beta blockers to reduce cardiac heart rate.
(c) Glucocorticoids: inhibit hormone production and decrease peripheral conversion from T4 to T3.</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Monitor VS including pulse rate and temperature</li>
<li>Monitor Cardiac rhythms</li>
<li>Provide a quiet environment</li>
<li>Administer antipyretics like paracetamol</li>
<li>Administer IV fluids to correct dehydration</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="goitre">GOITRE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goitre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Abnormal enlargement of thyroid gland due to inflammation or tumor that become visible</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mortality-and-morbidity">Mortality and Morbidity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mortality-and-morbidity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Most goitres are benign, causing only cosmetic disfigurement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Morbidity or mortality may result from compression of surrounding structures, thyroid cancer, hyperthyroidism or hypothyroidism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Female to male ratio : 4 : 1</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They are common in women than men</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-goiters">Classification of goiters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-goiters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Toxic goiter : a goiter that is associated with hyperthyroidism
Examples include : a. diffuse toxic goiter (graves disease)
b. toxic multinodular goiter and toxic adenoma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non toxic goiter: a goiter without hyperthyroidism or hypothyroidism. Examples are congenital goitre and physiologic goiter that occurs during puberty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non – toxic goiters</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>There are four types of Non Toxic goiters
a. Diffuse non-toxic goiter
b. Multinodular non-toxic goiter
c. simple goiter
d. uninodular goitre</p>
<p>A. Diffuse non – toxic goiter</p>
<ul>
<li>Develops during early stage of disease</li>
<li>The thyroid gland is diffusely enlarged</li>
<li>There is hypertrophy and hyperplasia of follicular cells.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-multinodular-non-toxic-goiter">B. Multinodular non-toxic goiter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-multinodular-non-toxic-goiter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Evolves as the disease becomes chronic</li>
<li>The gland develops nodules that vary in shape</li>
<li>Is the most common especially in older patients.</li>
<li>It's the most common cause of tracheal and oesophageal compression and may cause laryngeal nerve palsy..</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<p>C. simple goiter - There is no clear cause for enlargement of the thyroid which is usually smooth and soft.</p>
<p>d. Solitary nodular goiter (Plummers syndrome) - They are usually cystic or benign with a history of pain, rapid enlargement or associated lymph nodes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-of-non-toxic-goiters">Clinical features of non-toxic goiters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-non-toxic-goiters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Patients are asymptomatic presenting with a mass in the neck</li>
<li>If goiter is large, there will be compressive symptoms such as dysphagia (difficulty in swallowing)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-goitres">Causes of goitres<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-goitres" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertrophy caused by excess stimulation</li>
<li>Iodine deficiency</li>
<li>Hashimoto's thyroiditis</li>
<li>Goitrogens: are substances that suppress the function of thyroid gland by interfering with iodine uptake e. g cassava and sweet potatoes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-simple-goitre">Pathophysiology of simple goitre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-simple-goitre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>simple goiter may be caused by lack of iodine and intake of large quantities of goitrogenic substances</li>
<li>The pituitary gland produces thyrotropin or TSH, a hormone that controls the release of thyroid hormone from the thyroid gland.</li>
<li>Its production increases if there is subnormal thyroid activity, as when insufficient iodine is available for production of the thyroid hormone..</li>
<li>Increase in TSH courses overstimulation of thyroid gland leading to compensatory hypertrophy or enlargement</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thyroid function tests of thyroid stimulating hormone, thyroxine and triiodothyronine to determine whether a goitre is associated with hyperthyroidism, hypothyroidism or normal thyroid function</li>
<li>Chest and thoracic inlet x-rays to detect tracheal compression.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Measurement of thyroid antibodies to assess for thyroiditis.</li>
<li>Ultrasound to demonstrate whether the nodules are cystic or solid.</li>
<li>Thyroid scan to determine whether the nodule is malignant.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A goitre associated with normal thyroid function in pregnancy and puberty rarely requires intervention and patient needs to be reassured</li>
<li>Surgery if there is obstructive symptoms</li>
<li>In older patients Radioactive iodine therapy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications-for-surgery">Indications for surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications-for-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The possibility of malignancy where there is a history of rapid growth, pain, cervical lymphadenopathy or previous irradiation.</li>
<li>Pressure symptoms on the trachea.</li>
<li>Cosmetic reasons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thyroidectomy">THYROIDECTOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thyroidectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to surgical removal of the thyroid gland</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications-for-thyroidectomy">Indications for thyroidectomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications-for-thyroidectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Large goiter unlikely to respond to medications</li>
<li>Neoplasm of the thyroid</li>
<li>Correction of hyperthyroidism resistant to medications</li>
<li>Patients’ choice.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precautions-during-the-surgery">Precautions during the surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions-during-the-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Identification and preservation of recurrent laryngeal nerve, superior laryngeal nerve and parathyroid gland.</li>
<li>Unilateral damage to recurrent laryngeal nerve will result in post-operative hoarseness due to paralysis of one vocal cord.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Bilateral damage to both recurrent laryngeal will result in paralysis of both vocal cords, and it may cause acute airway obstruction.</li>
<li>Damage to superior laryngeal nerve is less noticeable because mobility of vocal cords is maintained</li>
<li>Removal of parathyroid gland will result in post operative hypoparathyroidism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-operative-preparation">Pre-operative preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-operative-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide a restful, quiet environment.</li>
<li>Regulate nutritional intake, that is, food should be high in carbohydrate and protein.</li>
<li>Pre-operative investigations.</li>
<li>Prepare the patient for surgery by sharing information, giving instructions on what to expect and the informed consent</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient must be restored to euthyroid state.</li>
<li>Pre-operative teaching should include comfort and safety measures.</li>
<li>Coughing and deep breathing exercises should be practiced including how to support the neck manually while turning in bed because this minimises stress on the suture line after surgery and exercises of the neck</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Medications that are used to restore euthyroid state are;</li>
<li>propylthiouracil is administered until signs of hyperthyroidism have disappeared.</li>
<li>A beta-adrenergic blocking agent (propranolol) may be used to reduce the heart rate and other signs and symptoms of hyperthyroidism</li>
<li>Iodine (Lugol’s solution or potassium iodide) is administered to reduce blood loss;</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="post-operative-management">Post operative management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-operative-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Set Oxygen, suction equipment and a tracheostomy tray at the bed side to be readily available in case airway obstruction occurs.</li>
<li>Position patient: Semi-Fowler’s, neck on neutral position to avoid tension on the neck sutures.</li>
<li>Assess patient every two hours for 24 hours for signs of haemorrhage or tracheal compression e.g. irregular breathing, neck swelling, blood on the anterior and posterior dressing.</li>
<li>Check for signs of tetany secondary to hypoparathyroidism e.g. tingling in toes, fingers or around mouth, muscular twitching.</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Monitor vital signs, temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess frequently for frequent airway obstruction. Significant irritation of or injury to both recurrent laryngeal nerve may result to bilateral vocal cord paralysis with airway obstruction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observe for signs of thyrotoxic crisis which include tachycardia, diaphoresis, increased blood pressure and anxiety</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer prescribed analgesics to control pain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer IV fluids</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-of-thyroidectomy">Complications of thyroidectomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-thyroidectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thyrotoxicosis crisis (thyroid storm) which is an acute but rare condition in which all the hyperthyroid manifestation are worsened and may include severe tachycardia, heart failure, hyperthermia, restlessness.</li>
<li>Recurrent laryngeal nerve damage which may lead to vocal cord paralysis.</li>
<li>Difficulty in breathing due to swelling of neck tissues, haemorrhage, haematoma formation.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Laryngeal stridor (harsh vibratory sound) may occur during respiration due to tetany from damaged or removal of parathyroid.</li>
<li>Early post-operative bleeding</li>
<li>Recurrent hyperthyroidism occurs in 1-3% within one year and then 1% per year</li>
<li>Hypothyroidism occurs in about 10% of patients within one year.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="recurrent-hyperthyroidism">Recurrent hyperthyroidism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recurrent-hyperthyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>All three treatments (radioactive iodine therapy, antithyroid medications, and surgery) share the same complications: relapse or recurrent hyperthyroidism and permanent hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>The rate of relapse increases in patients who had very severe disease, a long history of dysfunction, ocular and cardiac symptoms, large goiter, and relapse after previous treatment.</li>
<li>The relapse rate after radioactive iodine therapy depends on the dose used in treatment.</li>
<li>Hypothyroidism occurs in almost 80% of patients at 1 year and in 90% to 100% by 5 years for both the multiple low-dose and single high-dose methods.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parathyroid-disorders">PARATHYROID DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parathyroid-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypoparathyroidsm">HYPOPARATHYROIDSM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypoparathyroidsm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypo-secretion of parathyroid hormone</li>
<li>CAUSES: tumor, removal of the gland during thyroid surgery</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">PATHOPHYSIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Parathormone regulates calcium balance by increasing absorption of calcium from GI tract, bone resorption of calcium</li>
<li>deficiency of parathormone results in hypocalcaemia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment">ASSESSMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>if the facial nerve (immediately in front of the ear) is tapped, the client’s mouth twitches and the jaw tightens. This is called <strong>positive chvostek’s sign</strong>.</li>
<li>A positive <strong>trousseau’s sign</strong> may be elicited by placing a blood pressure cuff on the upper arm inflating it and waiting for 3 minutes.</li>
<li>The client is observed for spasm of the hand (carpopedal spasm) which is evidenced by hand flexing inward</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="presenting-features">PRESENTING FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presenting-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Numbness and tingling sensation on the face</li>
<li>Muscle cramps</li>
<li>(+) Trousseau's and (+) Chvostek's signs</li>
<li>Bronchospams, laryngospasms, and dysphagia</li>
<li>Cardiac dysrhythmias</li>
<li>Hypotension</li>
<li>Anxiety, irritability and depression</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions">NURSING INTERVENTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Monitor VS and signs of HYPOcalcemia</li>
<li>Initiate seizure precautions and management</li>
<li>Place a tracheostomy set. O2 tank and suction at the bedside</li>
<li>Prepare CALCIUM gluconate</li>
<li>Provide a HIGH-calcium and LOW phosphate diet</li>
<li>Advise client to eat Vitamin D rich foods</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypeparathyroidism">HYPEPARATHYROIDISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypeparathyroidism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypersecretion of parathyroid hormones</li>
<li>The main cause is tumor.</li>
<li>It is characterized by an excessive secretion of PTH resulting in hypercalcaemia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
