<li>In primary hyperparathyroidism, excessive secretion of parathyroid hormone (parathormone) results in increased urinary excretion of phosphorus and loss of calcium in the bones.</li>
<li>The bones becomes dematerialized as the calcium leaves and enters the blood stream.</li>
<li>Renal stones may develop because of an increase in serum calcium (hypercalcaemia).</li>
<li>The most common cause of primary hyperparathyroidism is an adenoma of one of the parathyroid glands</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>In secondary hyperparathyroidism, the parathyroid glands secrete an excessive amount of parathormone in response to hypocalcaemia, which may be caused by vit D Deficiency, chronic renal failure, large doses of thiazide diuretics, and excessive use of laxatives and calcium supplements</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms due to hypercalcemia: fatigue, muscle weakness, nausea, vomiting, consitipation, cardiac dysrhythmias</li>
<li>Renal damage due to deposition of calcium phosphate. eg renal calculi, obstruction, pyelonephritis, and renal failure</li>
<li>Musculoskeletal symptoms, joint pain, pathologic fracture, deformity, and shortening of the stature</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>provide high fluid intake to dilute serum calcium and urine calcium levels</li>
<li>Monitor VS, Cardiac rhythm, I and O</li>
<li>Administer prescribed diuretics. i.e Furosemide to lower calcium levels. Diuretic will act on the kidney to cause fluid loss and hence lower the possibility of kidney stone formation</li>
<li>provide food low in calcium</li>
<li>Monitor for signs of renal stones, skeletal fractures. Strain all urine</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-adrenal-medulla">DISORDERS OF ADRENAL MEDULLA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-adrenal-medulla" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pheochromocytoma">PHEOCHROMOCYTOMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pheochromocytoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pheochromocytoma">PHEOCHROMOCYTOMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pheochromocytoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pheochromocytoma is a benign tumor of adrenal gland.</li>
<li>Originates from the chromaffin cells of the adrenal medulla.</li>
<li>Adrenal medulla Produces catecholamines: adrenaline (epinephrine) and norepinephrine</li>
<li>The tumor causes Increased secretion of epinephrine and nor-epinephrine by the adrenal medulla</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>May occur at any age, but its peak incidence is between ages 40 and 50 years.</li>
<li>It affects men and women equally.</li>
<li>Because of the high incidence of pheochromocytoma in family members, the patient’s family members should be screened</li>
<li>It causes high blood pressure in 0.2% of patients with new onset of hypertension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The typical triad of symptoms comprises headache, diaphoresis (profuse sweating) and palpitations</li>
<li>Other symptoms include :</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Tachycardia</li>
<li>Weight loss, tremors</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia and glycosuria</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Abdominal pain</li>
<li>Vertigo</li>
<li>blurring of vision</li>
<li>Tinnitus</li>
<li>dyspnea.</li>
<li>Postural hypotension occurs in 70% of patients with untreated pheochromocytoma</li>
</ul>
<p>Assessment and Diagnostic Findings</p>
<ul>
<li>Pheochromocytoma is suspected if signs of sympathetic nervous system overactivity occur in association with marked elevation of blood pressure.</li>
<li>These signs can be associated with the “five Hs”: hypertension, headache, hyperhidrosis (excessive sweating), hypermetabolism, and hyperglycemia.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Measurements of urine and plasma levels of catecholamines are the most direct and conclusive tests for overactivity of the adrenal medulla</li>
<li>Measurements of urinary catecholamine metabolites (metanephrines [MN] and vanillylmandelic acid [VMA]) or free catecholamines are the standard diagnostic tests used in the diagnosis of pheochromocytoma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Alpha adrenergic blocking agents (eg, phentolamin [Regitine]) or smooth muscle relaxants (eg, sodium nitroprusside [Nipride]) to lower the blood pressure quickly.</li>
<li>Beta-adrenergic blocking agents, such as propranolol (Inderal), may be used in patients with cardiac dysrhythmias or those not responsive to alpha-blockers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-management">Surgical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The definitive treatment of pheochromocytoma is surgical removal of the tumor, usually with adrenalectomy (surgical removal of adrenal gland)</li>
<li>Bilateral adrenalectomy may be necessary if tumors are present in both adrenal glands.</li>
<li>Patient preparation includes control of blood pressure and blood volumes; usually this is carried out over 7 to 10 days</li>
<li>Phentolamine or phenoxybenzamine (Dibenzyline) may be used safely without causing undue hypotension</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Hydration before, during, and after surgery to prevent hypotension.</li>
<li>Manipulation of the tumor during surgical excision may cause release of stored epinephrine and norepinephrine, with marked increases in blood pressure and changes in heart rate.</li>
<li>use of sodium nitroprusside (Nipride) and alpha-adrenergic blocking agents may be required during and after surgery to control increases in catecholamine levels</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Corticosteroid replacement is required if bilateral adrenalectomy has been necessary</li>
<li>Corticosteroids may also be necessary for the first few days or weeks after removal of a single adrenal gland</li>
<li>Intravenous administration of corticosteroids (methylprednisolone sodium succinate [Solu-Medrol]) may begin the evening before surgery and continue during the early postoperative period to prevent adrenal insufficiency</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Monitor VS especially BP and document the vitals</li>
<li>Monitor for HYPERTENSIVE crisis: it is a severe increase in blood pressure that can lead to stroke and impairment of an organ</li>
<li>Avoid palpating the gland as it stimulates the tumor that can cause increased BP</li>
<li>Administer Anti-hypertensive agents like alpha-adrenergic blockers Phenoxybenzamine</li>
<li>Monitor blood glucose and urine glucose</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Promote adequate rest and sleep periods</li>
<li>provide HIGH calorie foods and Vitamins/mineral supplements</li>
<li>Prepare patient for possible surgery</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Post-operative management</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor vitals signs every 15 minutes until the patient is stable</li>
<li>Administer prescribed corticosteroid to prevent adrenal insufficiency.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Blood sugars and ECG monitoring until the patient is stable</li>
<li>Intravenous fluids, normal saline alternated with 10% dextrose to prevent hypotension</li>
<li>Monitor the drainage to check for the constant changes in drains. The discharge must be clear red and reducing daily</li>
<li>Provide the patient with a well balanced diet.</li>
<li>On discharge give health education on self monitoring of BP and regular check ups.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disorders-of-adrenal-cortex">DISORDERS OF ADRENAL CORTEX<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-adrenal-cortex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>ADDISON'S DISEASE</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="addison-s-disease">ADDISON'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#addison-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to adrenal insufficiency resulting from decreased secretion of adrenal cortex hormones, especially glucocorticoids and mineralocorticoids</li>
<li>Hypofunction of adrenal cortex</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Autoimmune destruction of the gland</li>
<li>Atrophy of the adrenal gland</li>
<li>surgical removal of both adrenal glands</li>
<li>Infections like Tuberculosis and histoplasmosis</li>
<li>Inadequate secretion of ACTH from the pituitary gland</li>
<li>Therapeutic use of corticosteroids</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Inadequate secretion of ACTH, autoimmune destruction of the gland or infections of the gland leads to decreased secretion of glucocorticoids and mineralocorticoids.</li>
<li>This results in hypoglycemia, weight loss, hyponatremia, hyperkalemia, hypovolemia and hypotension.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e44dbe41.jpeg" alt="img-54.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Damage to the adrenal cortex; progressive atrophy of gland.</li>
<li>Deficiency in cortisone and aldosterone</li>
<li>Imbalance of these hormones causes deregulation of important body functions that are potentially life-threatening.</li>
<li>Disease manifests itself when 90% of the adrenal gland is destroyed.</li>
<li>80% of cases have an autoimmune origin, 20% result from infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>GI disturbances</li>
<li>Muscle weakness, lethargy and fatigue</li>
<li>Hyponatremia</li>
<li>Hyperkalemia</li>
<li>Hypoglycemia</li>
<li>dehydration and hypovolemia</li>
<li>Increased skin pigmentation (bronze pigmentation) due to high levels of circulating ACTH</li>
</ol>
<p>ADDISON'S DISEASE</p>
<p>BRONZE
PIGMENTATION
OF SKIN
CHANGES IN
DISTRIBUTION
OF BODY HAIR

<p>HYPOGLYCEMIA

JMKLER</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-965e40ca.jpeg" alt="img-55.jpeg">
Fig. 2 Addison's disease - hyperpigmentation involving the palms of the hand.</p>
<p>Assessment and Diagnostic Findings</p>
<ul>
<li>The diagnosis is confirmed by laboratory test results.</li>
</ul>
<p>Laboratory findings include :</p>
<ul>
<li>low levels of adrenocortical hormones in the blood or urine and decreased serum cortisol levels</li>
<li>Decreased blood glucose (hypoglycemia) and sodium (hyponatremia) levels, an increased serum potassium (hyperkalemia) level and an increased white blood cell count (leukocytosis).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hydrocortisone is administered intravenously, followed with 5% to replace the cortisol hormones.</li>
<li>Vasopressor amines (epineprine) may be required if hypotension persists.</li>
<li>Hormonal replacement of aldosterone if necessary</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Monitor the patient for signs and symptoms indicative of <strong>addisonian crisis</strong>. These symptoms are often the manifestations of shock:
<strong>hypotension; rapid, weak pulse; rapid respiratory rate; pallor; and extreme weakness</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer prescribed hormonal hydrocortisone to replace adrenal insufficiency</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Monitor VS especially BP and document them</li>
<li>Monitor weight and I and O and document in the input output chart</li>
<li>Monitor blood glucose level and K+ levels to rule out hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Provide a high-protein, high carbohydrate and increased sodium intake</li>
<li>Avoid physical and psychological Stressors. These include exposure to cold, infection, and emotional distress</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>
<p>Educate the client regarding lifelong treatment, avoidance of strenuous activities, stress and seeking prompt consultation during illness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Initiate and maintain iv infusion of normal saline.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="addisonian-crisis">ADDISONIAN CRISIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#addisonian-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A life-threatening disorder caused by acute severe adrenal insufficiency</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precipitating-factors">PRECIPITATING FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Severe stress</li>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>Exposure to cold</li>
<li>surgery</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="presenting-features">Presenting features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presenting-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is characterized by cyanosis and the classic signs of circulatory shock: pallor, apprehension, rapid and weak pulse, rapid respirations and low blood pressure.</li>
<li>In addition, the patient may complain of headache, nausea, abdominal pain, and diarrhea and show signs of confusion and restlessness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hydrocortisone (Solu-Cortef) is administered intravenously, followed with 5% dextrose in normal saline</li>
<li>Vasopressor amines may be required if hypotension persists.</li>
<li>Antibiotics may be administered if infection has precipitated adrenal crisis in a patient with chronic adrenal insufficiency</li>
<li>lifelong replacement of corticosteroids and mineralocorticoids to prevent recurrence of adrenal insufficiency if adrenal gland does not recover.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Avoid physical and psychological stressors must be avoided. These include exposure to cold, overexertion, infection, and emotional distress</li>
<li>Administer IV Glucocorticoids, usually hydrocortisone and other prescribed medications</li>
<li>Monitor VS frequently, Monitor I and O, neurological status, electrolyte imbalances and blood glucose</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Administer IV Fluids : normal saline and 5% dextrose</li>
<li>Maintain bed rest to conserve energy</li>
<li>Health education on lifelong hormone replacement therapy.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cushing-s-syndrome">CUSHING'S SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cushing-s-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A condition resulting from the hyper-secretion of Glucocorticoids from the adrenal cortex</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Excessive use of corticosteroids</li>
<li>Tumor of the pituitary gland that produces ACTH and stimulates the adrenal cortex to increase its hormone secretion despite adequate amounts being produced</li>
<li>Primary hyperplasia of the adrenal gland.</li>
<li>Malignancies that produce ACTH</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cushing syndrome is caused by mechanism such as tumor of pituitary that produces ACTH that stimulates adrenal cortex to increase production of Glucocorticoids and androgens</li>
<li>When overproduction of the adrenal cortical hormone occurs, arrest of growth, obesity, and musculoskeletal changes occur along with glucose intolerance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Generalized muscle weakness and wasting because of excess protein catabolism</li>
<li>central obesity (truncal obesity)</li>
<li>Moon-face, due to fat deposit on the areas</li>
<li>Buffalo hump due to fat deposition</li>
<li>Easy bruisability due to thinned skin esp on the lower limb (along the tibia) that are slow to heal</li>
<li>Reddish-purplish striae on the abdomen, breast and thighs</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Hypertension because of Na+ and H2o Retention</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia</li>
<li>Osteoporosis</li>
<li>Amenorrhea or oligomenorrea</li>
<li>There is increased susceptibility to infection</li>
<li>There is an excessive growth of hair on the face (hirsutism) in women and other parts of the body</li>
<li>Irritability and depression</li>
<li>In male, there is gynaecomastia, erectile dysfunction and decreased sexual interest</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cushing-s-syndrome">CUSHING'S SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cushing-s-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-0d86ae58.jpeg" alt="img-56.jpeg"></p>
<table><thead><tr><th><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1483e917.jpeg" alt="img-57.jpeg"></th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id=""><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-fb001227.jpeg" alt="img-58.jpeg"><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="normal">Normal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#normal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cushing-s">Cushing's<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cushing-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ef4ccd2e.jpeg" alt="img-59.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-14f034f5.jpeg" alt="img-60.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Indicators of Cushing’s syndrome include:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>An increase in serum sodium and blood glucose levels</li>
<li>Decreased serum concentration of potassium,</li>
<li>Reduction in the number of blood eosinophils, and disappearance of lymphoid tissue</li>
<li>An overnight <strong>dexamethasone suppression test</strong> is the most used screening test for diagnosis of pituitary and adrenal causes of Cushing’s syndrome</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Surgery if the cause is tumor of the pituitary gland. Surgical removal of the tumor by trans-sphenoidal hypophysectomy is the treatment of choice and has a 90% success rate</li>
<li>Radiation of the pituitary gland</li>
<li>Adrenal ezyme inhibitors eg metyrapone, ketoconazole</li>
<li>Adrenalectomy is the treatment of choice in patients with primary adrenal hypertrophy</li>
<li>Tapering of corticosteroids if it was cause the problem</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Monitor I and O, weight and VS</li>
<li>Monitor laboratory values- glucose, Na, K and Ca2+</li>
<li>Provide meticulous skin care. Avoid USE OF ADHESIVE TAPE!!</li>
<li>Promote a relaxing, quiet environment for rest and sleep.</li>
<li>Provide a LOW carbohydrate, LOW sodium and HIGH protein diet</li>
</ol>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Protect the patient from infection by ensuring aseptic procedures. Avoid unnecessary exposure to others with infections</li>
<li>Health education on identification of signs of cortical sufficiency</li>
</ul>
<p>Hyperadrenalisms</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-hyperaldosteronism">Primary Hyperaldosteronism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-hyperaldosteronism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary hyperaldosteronism – excess aldosterone secretion which is independent of the renin-angiotensin system (Conn’s syndrome)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Aldosterone secreting adenoma</li>
<li>Bilateral hyperplasia of the cortex</li>
<li>Rarely carcinoma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Hypertension, hypokalemia, sodium retention, muscle weakness, paraesthesia, ECG changes, cardiac decompensation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aldosterone, by inducing renal distal tubular reabsorption of sodium, enhances secretion of potassium and hydrogen ions, causing hypernatremia, hypokalemia, and metabolic alkalosis.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mortality-morbidity">Mortality/Morbidity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mortality-morbidity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The morbidity and mortality associated with Conn syndrome, are primarily related to;</li>
</ul>
<p>1- Hypertension, especially if left untreated for many years, can lead to many complications, including heart disease (eg, coronary artery disease, congestive heart failure), stroke, and intracerebral hemorrhage (with very high blood pressure)</p>
<p>2-Hypokalemia, especially if severe, causes cardiac arrhythmias, which can be fatal</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-2ry-hyperaldosteronism">II- 2ry hyperaldosteronism:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-2ry-hyperaldosteronism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There is increased renin-angiotensin with increased aldosterone secretion;</li>
<li>CHF (congestive heart failure)</li>
<li>Liver cirrhosis and ascites</li>
<li>Nephrotic syndrome</li>
<li>Renal artery stenosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Clinical suspicions should be raised when</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension occur with hypokalemia.</li>
<li>Moderate to severe hypertension</li>
<li>Hypokalemia</li>
<li>Muscle weakness</li>
<li>Malaise</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Blood : Hypokalemia
Plasma aldosterone</li>
<li>Urine : Increase urinary potassium</li>
<li>Imaging : US
CT
MRI</li>
</ul>
